27th State Affairs Meeting of the Executive Yuan 74

Appoints Yan Deqing as Director of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board

Passes Measures to Inspect Mail for Smuggling of Narcotics

On the 1st, the 37th State Affairs Meeting of the Executive Yuan was held. Attendees included Song Ziwen, Wang Boqun, Li Shuhua, and Ma Fuxiang. Attending in a non-voting capacity were Chen Yi, Zheng Hongnian, Zhang Weihua, Fan Guang, Chen Shaokuan, and Song Ziwen, who presided over the meeting. Matters discussed included: (1) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs submitted a report stating that the terms of the ministry's inspectors sent to various provinces had expired. After careful evaluation, the ministry determined that their duties were still necessary and should not be terminated immediately. It seemed appropriate to extend their terms for another six months to facilitate their work. It requested review and approval for record-keeping. The decision was approved. (2) The Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Transportation, the Anti-Opium Commission, and the Ministry of Interior jointly submitted a report stating that they had been ordered to jointly and appropriately revise the measures to inspect mail for the smuggling of narcotics. After careful study and further revisions, they submitted the revised draft for review and approval. The decision was passed. (3) It was decided to appoint Yan Deqing as a director of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board. (4) It was decided to appoint Xu Guangyao, a member of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government and Director of the Construction Department, to concurrently serve as the Director of the Provincial Industry Department.

Panic Arises Again Among Overseas Chinese in Korea 75

Japanese Newspapers Incite Turmoil

Consul General Zhang Negotiates with the Korean Governor-General

A dispatch from Incheon: During the Korean riots last month, there were rumors that our country's Consulate General in Korea had been destroyed. In reality, Koreans had discussed this but did not carry it out. Recently, since the incident of Japanese residents in Qingdao violently assaulting Chinese people, the rumors have worsened. Rumors of members of the Japanese National Essence Society attacking our country's Consulate General have resurfaced, causing great panic. According to a special edition of the Japanese-language Keijo Nippo published on the 19th, there were false claims that Chinese people in Qingdao attacked Japanese people, resulting in sixty deaths and twenty injuries among members of the National Essence Society. Consul General Zhang Weicheng, upon seeing the report, immediately requested that the Korean Governor-General's Office issue an order to take preventive measures and telegraphed our country's consuls in Korea to contact local officials to protect overseas Chinese. On the 20th, it was rumored that the Consulate General had received threatening letters from Japanese people, stating roughly: (1) A suicide squad would be formed to attack the Chinese Consulate General. (2) Overseas Chinese in Korea would be ordered to leave Korean territory. After receiving these letters, Zhang personally went to the Governor-General's Office to request an order for protection and to ban the newspapers. The Governor-General's Office agreed to comply immediately. However, the rumors remain strong, and plainclothes police are heavily deployed near the consulate every night, still fearing danger. The overseas Chinese here are like startled birds. Those with capital are returning to China in droves. Wu Xiaotang, the director of the Guang Gang, who possesses assets of hundreds of thousands of gold, also returned to Guangdong with his entire family last week. The situation for overseas Chinese is deteriorating daily, and it is feared that they will never recover. (22nd)

Summary of the Gao-Shao Disaster Situation 76

Breaches in Gaoyou Difficult to Block

Rescued Refugees Arrive in Yangzhou One After Another

A dispatch from Yangzhou: The flood disaster in Shaobo and Gaoyou urgently needs relief. A record of the situation is as follows.

▲ Three breaches in the Shaobo levee have been blocked. After breaches occurred in the levees of Shaobo and Gaoyou, a massive flood disaster occurred. According to Section Chief Cheng of the Jiangdu Public Works Office, there were a total of twenty-one breaches of various sizes between Zhaoguan and Six Locks in Shaobo (several of which dried up and stopped flowing). The danger in Gaoyou was caused by the initial collapse of the Dangjun Wharf, followed by Yumatou, Miaoxiangkou, Qigongdian, Ershilipu, and Sanshilipu, totaling six breaches. They were deep and wide, with the largest being several hundred zhang and the smallest being sixty to seventy zhang, surpassing the Jiangdu section. Currently, Shao Fuchen, Director of the Jiangdu Public Works Office, is supervising workers and security team soldiers, procuring materials, and transporting them to Shaobo to block the breaches. As of August 31st, the Yangmujiang Wharf, Wanshou Palace Datong Wharf, and three other places had been completely blocked. The Nanda Wang Temple breach could also be completed that evening. Due to the deep water and severe disaster at the Gaoyou breach, it was difficult to start blocking it. Chief Engineer Qiu Jihao of the [blank] Office arrived in Yangzhou on the 31st and boarded the Jiangdu Public Works material boat on the 1st to inspect the situation and plan the blocking project.

▲ Officials Inspect the Disaster, Various Circles Distribute Relief. Zhu Ziqiao, a standing committee member of the National Government Disaster Relief Committee, arrived by plane on the 30th to inspect the disaster situation and then returned to Shanghai. On the morning of the 31st, Chairman Ye Chucang of Jiangsu Province also accompanied Cheng Jingsheng of the National Disaster Relief Committee on a small warship to inspect the disaster area in Shaobo and Gaoyou. Upon arriving in Shaobo, they met Security Director Li Mingyang, who had returned from Qingjiangnan, and also arrived in Shaobo Town. Supervisor Zhang Zhijiang, at 6:30 am on the 31st, led Secretary-General Sun Zhicheng, Deputy Chief of Staff Song Bangrong, Counselors Sun Yun and Chen Zemin, and several aides and guards, carrying dry rations and more than a thousand yuan in cash, on a boat from Xiannv Temple to the Shaobo and Gaoyou disaster areas to inspect the disaster and distribute relief along the way. It was reported that after inspecting Shaobo, they rested at the Xiaoguan Emperor Temple and then went north again. They carried many proclamations to prohibit lawless people from taking advantage of the disaster to loot and burn, in order to facilitate the relief of the disaster victims. In addition, the Red Swastika Society, in addition to transporting one hundred pieces of relief goods on the 30th and handing them over to Luo Zhizhi of the Chamber of Commerce to distribute them separately in Gaoyou, transported more than one hundred and thirty pieces of relief goods on the 31st, sending relief team members to join the Huaiyang Disaster Relief Association and transport them to the Qiaoshu Fan [blank] area in the Li River to help disaster victims. The County Chamber of Commerce also sent personnel to the disaster areas in Shaobo, Gaoyou, and the surrounding villages to distribute large amounts of relief supplies and engage in relief efforts. All the refugees, including more than one hundred and seventy men, women, and children, were transported by the Red Swastika Society, escorted across the river, and given money to go to their relatives and friends. On the morning of the 31st, forty-nine more people arrived, and in the evening, sixty-four more people arrived, who were distributed to various shelters for food and accommodation. Furthermore, the Jiangsu Flood Disaster Relief Association and the Jiangbei Flood Disaster Temporary Relief Association also sent personnel yesterday on four boats, Yuanli, Yongchang, Fengyu, and others, towing six barges, loaded with twenty dan of fried rice, twenty dan of white rice, thirty thousand Jingjiang chisels, and three thousand five hundred jin of sesame cakes, from the province to Fuyunmen in this city. They set sail at 4:00 am on the 31st to first go to Xinghua and then to Dongtai to distribute relief separately.

▲ The Water Level of the Canal Drops, Color Turns Green, and Smell is Fishy. The water level of the Yangzhou Canal has been falling for days. As of the 31st, the riverbank outside the city was one and a half feet or two feet higher than the water surface. However, the water color turned grayish-green and had a fishy smell. It was generally believed that this was caused by the flow of corpses from the disaster area. People were warned not to drink it.

Overview of the Flood Situation in Various Counties of Hubei (Continued 2) 77

Busan: Since the morning of July 4th, the Consulate in Busan, upon hearing of the riots in Incheon and Keijo, contacted the police station that day to take preventive measures. On the 5th and 6th, they requested the police station and the Tao Ting to telegraph the police stations in each county to make every effort to protect overseas Chinese. On the 7th, the Korean Director-General of Political Affairs passed through Busan on his way to Keijo. Consul Chen met with the Director-General to discuss severely cracking down on rioters. The Director-General replied that he would provide complete protection. By the 8th, the situation in Busan was also very tense. Although the shops were still operating as usual, Chinese women and children in various parts of the city took refuge in the consulate, numbering about sixty people. On this day, the glass windows of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce were smashed by rioters in two places. In the evening, small stones were thrown into the consulate garden. At 9:00 pm, Koreans gathered a crowd of about three hundred people in the open space on the left side of the consulate, threatening to attack the consulate. At this time, police had already been stationed at the street entrance outside the consulate, cutting off traffic. Despite the rain, the Koreans did not disperse. Later, the chief of police personally went to the consulate to direct the cavalry to drive away the crowd. However, the Koreans threw stones at the cavalry, causing them to retreat. In a critical situation, the military police were telegraphed. The Koreans dispersed only when the military police arrived on the scene, which was already late at night. At 3:00 am on the morning of the 9th, Liu Zhennian, an overseas Chinese merchant selling kimonos in Makinoshima, and Sun Zhenshu, a restaurant owner, were attacked by more than thirty rioters who smashed their doors and windows and threw all the goods in the store into the street. Overseas Chinese fled to Japanese residences. The police arrested eight rioters and detained them in the police station. Overseas Chinese were escorted to the consulate by the police to take refuge. On the evening of this day, about one hundred and sixty overseas Chinese merchants closed their businesses and took refuge in the consulate. On the evening of the 10th, Koreans gathered again in the street to the right of the consulate, numbering six to seven hundred people. They were dispersed by the military police. The situation was relatively stable on the 11th. After the consulate had earnest discussions with the Tao Ting on protection measures, it was decided to restore the business date of overseas Chinese. The Tao Fu and various halls replied that they had strictly ordered all places to make every effort to crack down on rioters and had summoned representatives from various civil groups to convey to the Koreans that they must be peaceful. The 12th was generally stable. The number of overseas Chinese taking refuge in the consulate, the Chamber of Commerce, and various firms was about three hundred and twenty men and about sixty women. As of the morning of the 15th, when Rong Bao arrived in Busan to inspect, a small number of people were still staying at the consulate. About four-tenths of those who opened stores and operated businesses had no accidents. They agreed that if there were no problems the next day, they would all open their stores and operate as usual. As for the various territories under the jurisdiction of Busan, according to reports from various parties, except for the destruction of goods at the Yuansheng Dongmen window shop of overseas Chinese merchants in Qingbe Dapu Village, only glass was broken in other places. As for the number of overseas Chinese injured in beatings, there were five people. Direct and significant losses are currently being investigated in detail.

Huangpi: The county was hit by continuous rainstorms, causing mountain floods. All thirteen embankments in the county successively collapsed. The eastern, western, and southern riverside areas, spanning more than sixty li, were completely submerged. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief. Xianning: Although the county is a mountainous area, continuous rainstorms and rising water in the outer rivers and lakes caused flooding of fields and crops. The disaster situation was most severe in the lakeside areas of the seventh and eighth districts, followed by the first, fourth, ninth, and tenth districts. The third and sixth districts were originally mountainous areas, but mountain floods caused the fields and houses to be washed away and damaged. (Relief measures) Temporarily allocated 300 dan of relief rice and telegraphed the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Gongan: Since spring, there has been more rain than sunshine in the county. The fields in each embankment, especially those at lower elevations, have been submerged for a long time. Later, heavy rain caused the higher elevations to flood as well. Embankments such as Tianbao, Tonghe, Hao Zhangen, etc., successively collapsed. Soybeans, wheat, rice, and hemp were submerged at the bottom of the water. Cries of hunger were heard everywhere, and huts were turned into ruins. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Sui County: The county was hit by continuous rain for more than twenty days, causing mountain floods. The water depth in the plains was more than one zhang. The residents, fields, and houses in the northwest river area were severely affected by submersion and collapse. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Jianli: The water accumulated within the county's levees was very deep, and most of the crops were submerged. Later, a breach in the new levee caused reverse flow, crossing Hong Lake and backfilling. Most of the county's dikes were broken. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

[Blank] County: The county had already been ravaged by war and communist disasters, making it a thorny and desolate place. This year, continuous rainstorms and floods have resulted in widespread suffering and cries of sorrow. The sight of this is heartbreaking. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Dangyang: The mud dams in the southeast, such as Zishajiadao, Liuhua, Hualipu, etc., were almost completely submerged due to the eruption of mountain floods. People, livestock, and houses were all in the water. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Zhijiang: The river water in the county flooded, and the county seat was flooded, with depths of several feet. Areas such as Shangbailizhou, Luzhou Embankment, Gonghe Embankment, and Changshou Embankment were low-lying, and the water flowing from the upper reaches was surging, while the lower reaches could not accommodate and drain it, resulting in a vast sea. Countless crops were submerged. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief.

Yidu: The county experienced months of continuous rain, and the embankments successively collapsed in many places. Countless fields, crops, people, and livestock were submerged. Tens of thousands of disaster victims were displaced. Starving corpses lined the roads, a tragic sight. (Relief measures) Telegraphed to the emergency relief association to find ways to provide relief. (To be continued)

Liu Guitang Flees to Liangshan 80

Shandong Troops and Militia Are Conducting a Joint Suppression

A dispatch from Jinan: After Liu Guitang broke through from Daming, he led his remnants into Shandong Province, passing through Guancheng, Fanxian, Puxian, and Yuncheng. Recently, he has taken refuge in Liangshan. In addition to government troops pursuing him, the militia of various counties along the way are also taking advantage of the situation to launch a joint attack. Liu's troops are fighting and retreating. Because he is very familiar with the terrain of the counties in western Shandong, he was ultimately able to flee to Liangshan. The pursuing troops currently include the 87th Brigade of Rong Guangxing, the 86th Brigade of Chen Dexin, and the cavalry brigade of Li Xuande. Gu Liangyou, the commander of the Western Shandong Militia, has also led his troops to join, gathering between Juye and Yuncheng to set up an encirclement. Gu Liangmin, commander of the 22nd Division, also went to the border between Juye and Yuncheng on the 27th to make arrangements before returning to Yanzhou. This morning (30th), he returned to Jinan from Yanzhou to report on the situation of Liu Guitang's troops. According to Gu, Liu Guitang's troops are hiding in the area south of Liangshan, numbering no more than five or six hundred. Currently, the main forces have gathered to block and intercept them, preventing them from fleeing elsewhere. The problem should not be too difficult to solve. Notorious local bandits in southern Shandong, such as Guo Maifeng, died of illness in Baiyan Village, south of Sishui County, a month ago. The remaining four to five hundred people are now operating in the Tianma Court and Budaigou area near Mount Meng. The 22nd Division and various independent battalions are stationed in Yanzhou. The 1st Regiment of Ning Chunxiao's 64th Brigade is stationed in Qufu, the 2nd Regiment of Lin Binghai's unit is stationed in Sishui, and Xie Shuxian's unit of the Southern Shandong Militia is stationed in Xintai, jointly carrying out the suppression. The cavalry brigade of the 15th Route Army, led by Ma Tengjiao, is stationed in Linyi, assisting in the suppression.

Mountainous Western Fangshan County in Shanxi Province Ravaged by Bandits 81

Every Business and Household in the Entire County Looted Without Exception

Total Losses Amounting to Approximately One Million Three Hundred to Forty Thousand Yuan

According to Reports from County Representatives Appealing to the Provincial Government

Taiyuan Dispatch: Bandits are rampant in Fangshan County, and the people are suffering greatly. Recently, representatives of the entire county's villagers, three in total, were publicly elected to come to the province to report on the bandit disaster to the authorities and various legal organizations, and to request relief. The following is a general account:

▲The Actual Situation of the Ravage: It is found that Fangshan County is located in a remote corner of the west, where bandits can easily hide. The mountains overlap, and it is difficult to eliminate their lairs. Of the 22 main villages in the county, the main and auxiliary villages that were ravaged by bandits this time reached as many as 25. All substantial businesses and larger villages were completely looted, and even the mules and horses of the farmers were taken away, and more than 30 people were kidnapped.

▲Fleeing to the Wilderness: Currently, the people of the villages are supporting the old and carrying the young, fleeing to the wilderness, sleeping in the open day and night, unable to return home, and unable to cultivate the fields. The county government's public security bureau has also been looted clean, and other businesses have all suffered damage.

▲The Fall of the City: Before the city fell, the bandits first looted in the Zhoujiagou area, numbering about seventy or eighty people. The local village chief immediately sent a "feather letter" to the county government. The county magistrate ordered the chief of the public security bureau to lead police to attack, but the chief of the public security bureau said that the police had been fighting bandits in Yukou for days and were exhausted, and could not set off immediately. Unexpectedly, at three o'clock that night, the bandits broke into the city and seized all the firearms of the county government and the public security bureau, and destroyed the prison, releasing all the prisoners.

▲The County Magistrate is Kidnapped: After the bandits destroyed the prison, they kidnapped the county magistrate, Hui Youfu, as well as county government personnel and tax collection officials, totaling twenty-five people. The bandits entered the city at three o'clock in the morning and did not leave until four o'clock in the afternoon. Throughout the day, they robbed, raped, and looted everything. It is also reported that the bandits seem to be organized. After looting, they split into several groups and fled in all directions. Moreover, the county has many mountains. After the bandits flee into the mountains, their movements are unpredictable. In addition to requesting the provincial government to order the bandit suppression army to thoroughly eliminate them, and because the autumn harvest has been ravaged by bandits, a disaster has occurred, they request prompt relief. The villagers' losses this time are very large, and the public losses are also not small. The finance bureau lost more than three hundred silver dollars, more than one thousand provincial paper dollars, and more than eight hundred yuan in lottery tickets in the bureau. The interest-bearing money in outside businesses is estimated at more than 13,000 yuan. The loss of equipment is estimated at more than 1,500 yuan. The loss of clothing of public officials in the bureau is estimated at more than 400 yuan. The first high school lost books, instruments, and other equipment, estimated at more than 1,500 yuan. The public security bureau lost equipment worth more than 1,200 yuan. The county party headquarters lost books and equipment, estimated at more than 1,000 yuan. Working comrades lost an estimated 700 yuan, plus 201 provincial dollars. The total loss for both public and private sectors is more than 1.1 million yuan. (27th)

Various Places Raise Funds to Help with Relief 82

▲Weihaiwei: Weihaiwei Public Security Bureau Chief Huang, Salt Affairs Bureau Chief Fei, and Li Yunqian of the YMCA, considering the water disasters in various provinces awaiting relief, specially convened a meeting of all sectors of Weibu at the YMCA on August 23 to discuss methods for relief. Many people attended, and it was decided to organize the Weihaiwei Various Provinces Water Disaster Emergency Relief Association. The inaugural meeting was held on the 25th, with 15 committee members, in order to conduct a large-scale fundraising campaign. Xu Yanmou, the Weihaiwei Management Commissioner, was elected as the chairman of the committee. Regarding fundraising methods, it has been decided to ask all amateur performers to perform for two days on September 5th and 6th, and to hold a dance and entertainment event for two days on September 12th and 13th. Donation booklets will also be printed and distributed to the countryside to quickly raise large sums of money to save the people.

▲Nagasaki: The Nagasaki branch of the Kuomintang recently joined the Consulate in Nagasaki to invite representatives of various organizations in Nagasaki to hold a joint meeting on August 25 to discuss disaster relief methods. It was unanimously decided to organize the "Nagasaki Overseas Chinese Various Provinces Water Disaster Relief Fundraising Association". The organization method includes five sections: general affairs, accounting, fundraising, publicity, and documentation. The representative assembly elected five fundraisers, each serving concurrently as the director of each section. A fundraising notice was printed and distributed, and the fundraisers went door-to-door to solicit donations from the overseas Chinese. It is reported that overseas Chinese are very enthusiastic about donating money for disaster relief, and it is estimated that several thousand yuan can be collected, which is enough to show the overseas Chinese's concern for their motherland.

Hong Jiong, the special commissioner sent by the central government to Anhui to inspect the water disaster, and engineer Chen Zhiding and investigators, arrived in Anhui a few days ago and consulted with the provincial government to divide into five groups for investigation. The committee members of each group have already departed from Anqing on the 27th. Central Committee member Qian Danwu and Provincial Committee member Wen Yi arrived in Wuhu today to first investigate the Wuhu disaster in detail, and then proceed to various counties in southern Anhui.

▲Since its establishment, the Wuhu Water Disaster Relief Association has raised more than 48,800 yuan for relief. The Wudangfan Five County Righteous Relief Association previously publicly elected Mr. Zhai Zhanzheng to go to Beijing and Shanghai to raise funds. However, since the wind disaster the day before yesterday, the deaths and losses of the villagers in the townships have been even greater. County Magistrate Yu personally went to the townships yesterday to investigate. Some disaster victims were perched on trees calling for help, and the situation was particularly tragic. Relief is urgently needed. ▲Since Anhui banned rice exports, one party immediately carried out rice registration in order to prepare for the people's food supply. Unexpectedly, some unscrupulous merchants still took advantage of the name of military rice to smuggle it out, in large quantities. As a result of the registration, there are only 60,000 shi of rice in Wuhu, and the people's food has become panic-stricken. Therefore, the rice registration office decided to set up a rice export inspection office to strictly prohibit exports. Those who conceal and fail to register will be confiscated immediately and used as relief rice.

▲Since the major floods in southern Anhui, bandits have risen up. Residents of Wuhu's opposite Jiang Wuwei and other counties have fled completely. Even on the Wuhu River, bandit ships often block and rob travelers. Yesterday morning, the 171st Brigade Command stationed in Wuhu reported that bandits were taking boats across the river to rob. Therefore, a platoon of soldiers was dispatched, led by Deputy Officer Liu, to go by boat. They encountered the bandits in the heart of the river, and both sides opened fire for an hour. One bandit was injured on the spot, and five bandits were captured alive, along with a bandit ship and box guns. They were all escorted ashore and executed by firing squad on the Jianggan River. The brigade headquarters issued a notice announcing the process of suppressing the bandits.

▲The Datong Chamber of Commerce went on strike due to a conflict with the police. Huang Deji, the former chairman of the General Chamber of Commerce, is still in custody. Huang is a graduate of Jindai University. He runs Qinghehao in Datong. Recently, due to the flood, he took refuge in a Jiangnan hotel. He witnessed the Public Security Bureau forcing the collection of opium lamp donations at the hotel. Huang came forward to dissuade him, which led to his detention. In order to rescue Huang, the business community eventually went on strike. The Chamber of Commerce has now submitted a report to the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce, which will be forwarded to the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, requesting a thorough investigation to comfort public opinion. (30th)

Wuxi 87

Explosion of Explosives Box: One Worker Dead and Three Injured: The earthwork project on the Xiyi Road, Meidong Section, has been underway for more than a month since its start. The mountain opening project is contracted by the Xiehe Construction Company. The office is located in Meiyuan Lüjiang. Yesterday, at 5:00 am, four mountain opening workers from the company, Wu Youlin, Hui Jinshui, Shu Zhangsen, and Zhou Zhengren, were having dinner in a workshop about five li from the office. Wu took an explosives box and used it as a stool, causing the explosives to detonate. With a loud bang, smoke filled the air. Wu and the other three were injured in the explosion. Wu Youlin could not bear the pain and crawled to the edge of Taihu Lake and jumped into the lake to commit suicide. The body has not yet been recovered. The other three were taken to the hospital by company officials. Hui and Zhou suffered minor injuries, while Shu Zhangsen was seriously injured and his life was in danger.

Rice Boat Robbed, Two Suspects Arrested: Shi Dachang Rice Store in Yangxiang Town, Yixing County, entrusted boatmen Zhu Jinfu and Zhu Jinshou brothers to transport 140 shi of indica rice to Hengdachang Rice Store in Santiliqiao, Beitang, for sale to Wuxi. They received 805 yuan. At around 8:00 pm the day before yesterday (31st), a sampan suddenly came, and two bandits jumped out, their faces smeared with black ash, holding flashlights and sharp knives. At that time, the boatmen Zhu Jinfu brothers had gone ashore to bathe. Only Zhu's wife, Wang, and their children were left on the boat. After the two bandits boarded the boat, they tied Wang with ropes and forced her to tell them where the money was hidden. The 805 yuan for the rice was completely robbed. Afterwards, the Zhu Jinfu brothers returned to the boat after bathing and learned of the incident. They reported it to the Fifth Public Security Bureau. Director Peng immediately sent a police officer to pursue the bandits. Wu Zhengrong, the chief of political police of the county government, and Xue Furui, the captain of the criminal investigation team of the Public Security Bureau, also arrived at the scene one after another to investigate. Suspect Wang Laohai was arrested at Tonghui Bridge. At 2:30 am, another suspect, Jiang Xihai, was arrested in Jieguanting Lane. They were immediately taken to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Parricide Case Clarified by Examination: Zheng Genda, a villager in Zhengjia Alley, District 16, Dumenli, 92nd map, was recently beaten on the head with a dry tobacco pipe by his eldest son, Chunquan, causing his skull to shatter. He died the next day from his injuries. Later, Chunquan prepared a coffin and hastily buried him. Zhou, the chief prosecutor of the County Court, learned of the incident and sent judicial police chief Li Renzhen to the village to secretly investigate. He also took the murderer, Zheng Chunquan, to the court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Du, accompanied by Coroner Wang, took a car to Shitangwan and transferred to a civilian boat to the scene of the corpse. The coffin of Zheng Genda was opened for examination. It was confirmed that he died after being injured and passing away. After Prosecutor Du re-examined the evidence, he ordered the corpse to be re-coffined and buried. The murderer, Zheng Chunquan, was taken to the court, shackled, and imprisoned.

Letter

Letter from Lieshan Coal Mine General Corporation 96

Dear Editor: In the article on Susong County in your newspaper on the 22nd of this month, "The town of Xixi was submerged in more than 200 villages," it stated that "the cause was the Lieshan Coal Mine dam blocking the water, causing the rivers in Zhonggu Village, Beigu Village, and Nangu Village to flood and have nowhere to return." It has been verified that the Zhu Ji Dam of our mine has been opened and dismantled every year in the autumn when the water rises to prevent floods and facilitate transportation. At the beginning of July this year, it was dismantled due to a sharp rise in river water. As for the Wangjiazhai Dam, it was washed away by the water on the night of July 5, and the villagers demolished it on behalf of the company on the same day. Our mine did not prohibit it. The Xixi flood occurred in August. Our mine's wells and coal piles were submerged, and most of the factory was destroyed, resulting in heavy losses. It has been a full month since the opening of the dam. Moreover, the water volume in the Sui River was already several feet higher than the dam surface in July. Even if the dam was not dismantled, it would have been washed away long ago. The cause of the Xixi flood was attributed to our mine's river dam, which is obviously not consistent with the facts. Please correct it, we would be very grateful.

Educational News

Special Report

Future Focus of Vocational Education 97

Yang Weiyu

The failure of past education has become a common consensus. Since the Ministry of Education explicitly ordered the promotion of vocational education in April of this year, the atmosphere in the education sector has been refreshed. Since the National Congress determined the educational implementation plan to increase vocational schools as much as possible, the center of the education sector has undergone a major change. As of 1931, national school surveys and statistics are still unavailable. However, based on what is known in Jiangsu Province and Shanghai alone, the number of newly added vocational middle schools has reached more than fifty, and the number of ordinary middle schools that have added vocational subjects is not yet counted. If all twenty-eight provinces and directly governed cities are combined, the number must be very considerable. The development of vocational education can be said to be flourishing today. However, this is only a special expansion in appearance. If we investigate its essence, I am afraid it may not be so easy and fast. Therefore, the future focus of vocational education is definitely not on how to promote it, how to develop it, but on how to enrich it and how to adapt it. In other words, it is not about expanding the quantity, but about enriching the quality.

Today, the Ministry of Education is gathering experts and relevant representatives from various departments to discuss various issues of vocational education and make a comprehensive design. This is truly a fundamental plan and a matter of urgency. The promotion of vocational education in our country did not start today. Vocational schools are visible in various provinces, and vocational subjects are offered in senior high schools everywhere. However, most of the graduates are still not suitable for practical life, and graduates from schools are still unemployed in society. There is no other reason for this than that the settings are inappropriate, the objectives are uncertain, and the facilities lack standards. For the most part, they exist in name only and lack substance. Therefore, the statistical tables of schools in various provinces, cities, and counties show the number of vocational schools and vocational subjects in senior high schools, but the results are no different from those of ordinary schools. If this is taken as promoting vocational education, it is tantamount to destroying vocational education. Now that the Ministry of Education has seen this and has various designs, it is certainly very different from the previous lack of standards. The reason why I would like to add a word is that having a law is better than having no law, but a law that does not adapt to the environment and the times is also equivalent to having no law.

In recent months, I have often received information from comrades in various places, saying that when they wanted to run a middle school and applied for registration, the education departments ordered them to run vocational programs. Ordinary middle schools wanted to become vocational schools and generally set up accounting or horticulture elective courses. The departments then ordered them to reorganize into commerce or agriculture programs... The departments are implementing administrative orders and promoting vocational education, and their intentions are commendable. However, it is miserable for most school operators. Therefore, in order to comply with the orders, they have to reorganize and change subjects one after another, without having time to consider how to find a way out in the future or how to prepare now. In this situation, it is unlikely that they can avoid being nominal. Therefore, I believe that the Ministry of Education should at least pay attention to the following issues when stipulating the standards for vocational education facilities:

1. Adapt to the local environment and provide more opportunities for experimentation and research. The laws and regulations of education in European and American countries are certainly not without them, but they do not find it difficult to implement. Scholars should leave room for activities in each province to apply and opportunities to experiment.

2. Subdivide subjects in detail and be specific. There are several subjects in agriculture, and even more subjects in industry. Even commerce can be divided into several subjects. Allow school operators to freely set up subjects without affecting the standards.

3. Strictly define the standards for equipment. It is known to everyone that agricultural and industrial subjects should have appropriate equipment. Why is it different for commerce subjects? I have often heard that various provinces are eager to run vocational schools and run commerce subjects regardless of environmental needs, thinking that they are easy to set up. This is a fundamental mistake and should be regulated with standards.

4. Indicate the direction of career prospects. The greatest benefit of vocational schools is that they can provide career prospects. If, three years later, those who are now running vocational schools are still seeking career prospects and cannot find them, it will be a failure of vocational education. How to seek career prospects and how to broaden career prospects depends on the instructions of the designers of the Ministry of Education.

5. Stipulate the necessary conditions for establishing a school. The quality of a school depends not only on compliance with laws and regulations, but also on whether the organization is sound. When establishing a vocational school, it is advisable to investigate whether the establishment of subjects is appropriate, whether the equipment is complete, and whether the funding is sufficient. It would be very dangerous to take the compliance of its format as the standard for approval.

As for how to compile the curriculum and teaching materials, what are the standards for school facilities, etc., the designers have already considered them, so I will not repeat them.

The Songjiang County Fee Dispute Movement Temporarily Comes to an End 100

Schools to Reopen with Reluctance on September 1st

The budget for Songjiang County schools for the 20th year has long been explicitly approved. Since Commissioner Xu came to Songjiang for investigation, the Education Department suddenly made major cuts again. Teachers and staff of county middle and primary schools organized a joint association of middle and primary school teachers and staff to strive for it and decided to postpone the opening of school to wait for a solution. The details have been recorded in detail in this newspaper. It is now known that the County Education Bureau repeatedly telegraphed to the provincial government for requests and went to the province to present the difficulties. The Education Department has expressed its approval. After the Director returned to Songjiang, he sent two letters to the teachers and staff, advising them to open school. The County Education Association also sent a public letter to the Joint Association, asking them to prioritize the studies of more than 20,000 students and open school first. The funding problem will be fought for, etc. After the Joint Association approved the letter, it held a general meeting on the 30th, and the majority decided to open school with reluctance on September 1st. The declaration is recorded as follows:

Since the education funds of this county have been cut twice in the 19th year, the schools have been stretched to the limit. Considering the importance entrusted by the Education Bureau, the eager expectations of the people of the country, and the precious time and studies of 20,000 students, we dare not slack off, and we strive to maintain it in order to plant the foundation of the country and fulfill the obligations of the people. Unexpectedly, since investigator Xu came to Songjiang to investigate, the Education Department has greatly cut the education funds of this county. It is difficult to maintain even the current level, let alone develop it. Although we want to support it, we are more than willing but lack the strength. Therefore, we organized this association to strive for it. We have called for help through official documents and sought assistance from all sides. We are still afraid that it will not be enough, so we have expressed our intention to postpone the opening of school. The people of the country know that this move of this association is not an option, and they do not criticize us, but instead provide assistance. This is not only the private feeling of the colleagues, but also the blessing of Songjiang education. Previously, the Education Bureau, considering our difficulties, repeatedly telegraphed to the provincial government on both days, and the Education Department has agreed to maintain the approved budget, except that the funds for the senior departments of primary schools still need to be reduced. The Director also went to the province on the day to present the difficulties and asked to maintain the approved budget and send letters to all schools to open school on time to await further instructions. The Education Association also sent a letter to advise opening school first, and the funding problem will be fought for. This association is afraid of wasting the time and studies of 20,000 students, undermining the foundation of the country, and failing the good intentions and high expectations of the Education Bureau, the Education Association, and the people of the country. Although the original intention has not been fully realized and the solution has not been satisfactory, we dare not delay opening school on September 1st in order to avoid great slander. The funds for the senior departments of primary schools still need to be fought for to be exempt from reduction. We still hope that people from all walks of life will continue to lend a hand to achieve success. Please understand our private intentions.

Recent Situation of Fudan University 106

The Ministry of Education Instructs the School of Science Not to Change its Name

The Department of Education Adds a Normal Specialization

Jiangwan Fudan University opened on September 1st. Registration will begin today and tomorrow, and classes will officially start on the 7th. About 1,500 new and old students have enrolled. More than 30 professors have been newly hired in each department this semester, such as Chen Junde, a graduate of the University of London and Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, who was hired by the Department of Municipal Administration to teach Municipal Finance, Zhuang Bingquan, an engineer of Shanghai Kaiyi Company and a graduate of Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute in the United States, to teach Municipal Engineering, Dai Junliang was hired by the Department of Law to teach General Theory of Debt Compilation, Xu Dongfu, editor and interviewer of the English Shanghai Times, was hired by the Department of Journalism to teach English Composition, He Ziheng, editor of International News and Qingguang of Shishi News, was hired to teach International Issues, Sun Lianggong, Director of the Chinese Literature Department, went to Japan for a tour, and Xie Liuyi, Director of the Journalism Department, was hired to serve concurrently as the director. Li Quanshi, Dean of the School of Business, and Wu Songgao, Dean of the School of Law, have all returned to the school this semester as full-time professors. Most of the graduates of the Department of Civil Engineering of the school have served in important engineering positions in the country, and many have been registered as industrial technicians in the Ministry of Industry. The school previously thought that the department was located in the School of Science, which was not very appropriate in name. It applied to the Ministry of Education to change its name to the School of Science and Technology. Now it has received Instruction No. 3359 from the Ministry of Education, which states that the Department of Civil Engineering of the school should be located in the School of Science and there is no need to change the name of the School of Science to the School of Science and Technology. In addition, the school has added a normal specialization in the Department of Education, which has been approved by the same instruction.

Ping Gao Huimin Wins the First Singles

Chinese and foreign ladies and gentlemen went to watch one after another. Before 4:00, the stands were full of young men in suits and modern girls, exuding fragrance. Beijing players Yokota, Shi Changli and Tianjin players Uchida and Kuwahara arrived at the court first to practice. The doubles match started at 4:00. The result of the three-game match was that Beijing lost two to one. The second was the singles match between Ping Gao Huimin and Tianjin Wu Shaoxiang. After a long battle, Wu Shaoxiang was defeated 2-0. The third match was another doubles match. The Tianjin representatives were the Long Qian brothers, and the Ping representatives were the Sa brothers. Both sides were evenly matched. After a great battle of two hundred rounds, no winner was determined, and it was already dark, so the cadre of the court announced the end of the game. The battle situation is recorded as follows:

First Doubles 110

Uchida Kuwahara (Tianjin) 6|4 4|6 6|4 Shi Changli Yokota (Beijing)

Three-quarters of the strong players on both sides are Japanese, and the remaining one is the veteran Shi Changli, who dominated Pingjin a few years ago. Before Lin Baohua and Wu Shaoxiang came to Tianjin, Shi had long held the position of leader of the alliance, and although he is old this year, he is still strong. In yesterday's battle, his strength was no less. His assistant, Mr. Yanchu, is young and energetic, very similar to Qingying player Yamada, who came to Tianjin earlier. The Tianjin player Kuwahara is brave and steady, and has gained a concrete understanding of Murakami. Before the battle, both sides were evenly matched and gained something. In the second set, Ping's team was still sluggish at the beginning. After the third game, Shi Changli's spirit suddenly rose, and his offense and defense were as he wished. He won three consecutive games and then won two games again, so he reversed the defeat with 4 to 6. In the third set, the two sides fought in a mixed battle for a long time, and the winner was not determined. Ping won three games at the beginning, and Tianjin retaliated. Afterwards, they came and went. Finally, Kuwahara's pressing ball was successful, and they won again with 4 to 6. The results are as follows:

First Singles 111

Gao Huimin (Ping) 6|4 7|5 Wu Shaoxiang (Tianjin)

Wu Shaoxiang hits the ball with his left hand with strength and strength. Gao Huimin is the first master in Beijing. He is tall and jade-like, and it is most convenient to press the ball. Recently, he has learned a skill and is good at winning with spin balls. The ball is light and powerless when hit, and it will float slightly when it hits the opponent's position, making it impossible for the other side to return it. If it is too far away from the formation, it is not easy to catch. It was quite effective at first, but was later seen through by Wu and was controlled instead. In the first set, Gao sailed smoothly and won three consecutive games. Wu quickly counterattacked and also won two games, but Gao's morale was in full swing and he finally lost with 6 to 4. In the second set, the two sides engaged in a short-range attack. Gao won three games at the beginning, and Wu tried to save the situation and also won three games. Later, the record was actually created as five to four. Wu won a set. Afterwards, Wu had a chance to win another ball, that is, to win the whole set. Unfortunately, the time was not right, and it passed quickly. In the end, he lost badly with 7 to 5.

Local News

Japanese Navy Abduction Case 116

City Government Submits Second Protest

Regarding the abduction case by the Japanese Navy that occurred on August 12th, the City Government submitted its second protest yesterday. The original letter stated that it was deeply regrettable that the letter of August 20th deflected responsibility for the Mayor's protest against the Japanese Navy soldiers' abduction and detention of Chinese citizens. It was noted that regarding the goods of Japanese merchants mistakenly seized during the recent public movement, the Mayor, upon receiving reports, had already ordered investigations and returns. He had also responsibly stated that if the public acted carelessly and endangered the lives and property of foreigners, he would certainly take legal action. When your Consul-General visited previously, he was informed face-to-face. However, during the process of handling the case by both sides, your country's Navy disregarded our country's measures and rashly abducted and detained Chinese citizens within Chinese territory, acting in a tyrannical and arbitrary manner. This clearly shows disrespect for our country's sovereignty and violation of international conventions. As for the claim that the Japanese Navy's actions were intended to assist public security and maintain order, this government has the responsibility to protect the lives and property of foreigners within its jurisdiction according to law and treaty, and it does not allow others to overstep their boundaries and act on its behalf. In light of the previous circumstances, we reiterate the previous situation and protest again, requesting that you investigate the previous letter promptly and provide a reply.

Li Dezhao's Remarks on Suppressing the Communists 117

The Future is Very Optimistic

Li Dezhao, former Chief of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, has now been transferred to the Party and Government Committee of the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters. He returned to Shanghai from Nanchang yesterday. Reporters from various newspapers visited the garrison headquarters to inquire, meeting Li shortly after entering. They inquired about the situation on the front lines. His conversation with reporters is recorded as follows: (Reporter) How is the situation of suppressing the bandits in Jiangxi? (Li) Since the Commander-in-Chief arrived in Jiangxi to suppress the bandits, the spirit of the various armies has been greatly enhanced, and they are invincible. Important bandit strongholds such as Guangchang, Ningdu, Xiaobu, Wangpi, Longgang, and Donggu Xingguo have been recovered one after another. The strength of the Red bandits has long been reduced by more than half. The remaining bandits have scattered in all directions. Currently, there are no substantial bandit forces in eastern and western Jiangxi. Only a small number of remnants remain near Xingguo and Ningdu in southern Jiangxi. However, they are also lurking in the mountains, afraid to emerge. When the National Army goes to suppress them, they flee through small paths. Even if airplanes drop bombs into the forest, they are willing to endure the sacrifice rather than escape. The reason why they cannot be completely eliminated for the time being is because of this. But this is a matter of time. It is said that the National Army's suppression of bandits is like a lion hunting a rabbit. Although the rabbit is cunning, it is surrounded on all sides, and its range of escape is extremely small. Eventually, it will be caught one day. The reason why previous bandit suppression efforts were ineffective was that various parties excessively promoted the Communists, saying how formidable they were, causing the army to be apprehensive and easily taken advantage of. In fact, the bandit army lacks pay and ammunition, and it lacks training. In every aspect, it is inferior to the National Army. If they were to fight on a plain, they would have been wiped out long ago. However, they have one advantage that the National Army does not have, that is, they dare to kill people to intimidate the people. As for the inconvenience of transportation, the National Army certainly feels the difficulty, but they are no different. The current headquarters is rushing to repair roads, starting construction in sections, and setting a deadline for completion. It is estimated that there are three road construction agencies in Jiangxi Province, namely the Provincial Government's Highway Bureau, the Military Road Bureau directly under the headquarters (using soldiers to build roads), and the Labor Relief Road Construction Bureau of the Party and Government Committee (using disaster victims to build roads). In the future, when the roads are completed, transportation will be convenient. The remaining Red bandits will either be beaten to death or starve to death. Therefore, the future of bandit suppression is very optimistic. (Reporter) How is the work of post-disaster relief in the bandit areas? (Li) The headquarters has established a Party and Government Committee. Forty-three of the eighty-one counties in Jiangxi have been designated as bandit suppression areas and are under its jurisdiction. They are further divided into nine districts, each with a district branch of the Party and Government Committee. Each county also has a county branch to handle post-recovery affairs in the recovered areas. Party and government affairs are under its control. The work of the Party and Government Committee can be divided into three parts: (1) Regarding Party affairs, planning and guiding the organization and activities of Party and mass organizations in the bandit suppression areas, propaganda, training, and other methods. Regarding civil self-defense, guiding and urging the implementation of the Baojia system in the bandit suppression areas, household registration, the reorganization and expansion of self-defense teams, and the recruitment of refugees for training and self-government. (3) Regarding disaster relief, planning for the relief of disaster victims in the bandit areas (currently divided into emergency relief, work relief, and agricultural relief), the reorganization of land and land taxes, the determination of property rights, and the restoration of rural areas (currently planning to establish farmers' banks and cooperatives). The above items have all been formulated by the respective departments and design committees, and personnel have been assigned as district commissioners and county magistrates to start work. (Reporter) How is Commander-in-Chief Chiang's activity in Jiangxi? Are some of the external rumors true? What is the purpose of this trip to Wuhan? (Li) The Commander-in-Chief is extremely busy handling military and political affairs. In addition to inspecting the front lines from time to time, he is always in the headquarters day and night and rarely goes out. Only at dusk does he go to the Guanao Pavilion behind the headquarters to rest. The pavilion is in the lake, and the scenery is quite good. Nanchang is hot and humid, and the headquarters is even more so. The Commander-in-Chief braves the summer heat on his expedition. The only thing he relies on for comfort is this pavilion. There are many rumors outside, and I only learned about them after leaving Nanchang. All of them are unfounded and cannot be believed. As for this trip to Wuhan, it is to inspect the floods. (Reporter) Has Chief of Staff Xiong's health recovered? Is it true that he will be appointed as the chairman of Jiangxi or a certain province? (Li) Xiong's injury has fully recovered. His right foot limps, but not as much as before. His spirit is excellent. He eats three bowls of brown rice for each meal. Because the headquarters is small, he rents a civilian house nearby. He goes to the headquarters at six o'clock every morning and only returns at eight o'clock, reading telegrams and writing notes. He has almost no spare time. He and the Commander-in-Chief are both extremely busy people. Now that he is the Chief of Staff, I am afraid he will not have time to take on the chairmanship. There is also this rumor in Nanchang, but it is not as prevalent as in Nanjing and Shanghai. I do not know if it is true. At this point, the reporter, feeling that Li had just arrived at the department, did not want to talk for too long, so he bid farewell and left. It is said that Li will return to Nanchang within days.

Disaster Relief from All Sectors Yesterday 118

City-Run Disaster Relief Shelter Established

In recent days, there has been a considerable number of disaster victims from various provinces arriving in Shanghai. Coincidentally, the city-run shelter was also established yesterday, providing a temporary place for the disaster victims who narrowly escaped death. However, as the weather gradually turns cold, the threat of epidemics is concerning. Those handling relief efforts should pay close attention to hygiene and cold-weather equipment. Here is a summary of what was heard yesterday:

News from the National Government Flood Relief Committee 119

▲ Solicitation by the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group

The Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the National Government Flood Relief Committee, in order to prepare for the selection of personnel to work in the disaster areas, is soliciting physicians and nurses to volunteer to go to the various disaster areas to assist in medical relief, injections, and hygiene and epidemic prevention, for a minimum of two months. During the work period, the committee will provide living expenses and travel expenses, and may also provide salaries as appropriate. Those who are willing should state (1) qualifications, (2) age, (3) gender, (4) experience, (5) current position, and detailed address in their letters and send them to the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the Flood Relief Committee at 1 Jiujiang Road, Shanghai C. The group will then send separate letters of invitation to determine the overall deployment of work.

▲ Plan of the Disaster Area Work Group

The Disaster Area Work Group of the National Government Flood Relief Committee has drafted a work plan for the disaster areas for the committee's adoption. The main points are recorded as follows: (1) The Disaster Area Work Group shall dispatch representatives to all densely populated areas within the disaster areas to supervise all relief matters. For the convenience of handling affairs and improving work efficiency, these supervisors should liaise with local people to achieve cooperation. (2) The expenses required for the office work of the local disaster relief committees and accommodation will be planned by the respective committees locally, and the Flood Relief Committee will provide subsidies as necessary. (3) The local disaster relief supervisors shall cooperate with the local people to accommodate the disaster victims in temples and sheds. For those disaster victims who lack clothing and food, the supervisors shall plan for food and assist the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group in implementing the disaster area health plan. Priority should be given to hiring local disaster victims for construction projects such as building dikes and cleaning streets in the disaster areas. (4) Divide the disaster victims into two categories within the shortest possible time: (A) those who can find work and support themselves, and (B) those who cannot support themselves and need help. The disaster victims in category B will be moved by the committee to the planned work locations. (5) Organize engineers to supervise all post-disaster work. (6) When the post-disaster plan is complete and work can begin, the disaster area workers will be handed over to the engineers for use. (7) Post-disaster of farmland: (A) Plan how to distribute seeds and how to implement it. (B) Establish rural cooperatives to prepare for local bankers to lend money to farmers for the purchase of cattle, livestock, and agricultural tools.

▲ Zhu Qinglan Plans to Depart with Staff

It is reported that Zhu Qinglan, Director of the Disaster Area Work Group, plans to depart for the disaster areas in the next few days, accompanied by several staff members who have experience in relief and have cooperated with Zhu in the past, to select sites to organize model work areas. Their scope of work is the same as that of the work areas already established in Hankou. It is believed that after these personnel have gained sufficient experience in the model work areas, they will be sent to designated areas to be responsible for supervising relief work. It is believed that, with this method, relief work can be expected to spread to the disaster areas throughout the country in the shortest possible time.

▲ Emergency Relief Association Cables to Various Provinces to Distribute Relief Funds

The Shanghai Fundraising Emergency Relief Association for Flood Disasters in Various Provinces telegraphed the governors of the seven provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Henan, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi and the provincial relief associations, saying that the fourth meeting of the Standing Committee of the Association resolved to allocate 20,000 yuan each to Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, and Jiangsu for emergency relief, 10,000 yuan each to Jiangxi and Zhejiang, and 30,000 yuan to Henan. Mr. Zhu Ziqiao was publicly recommended to distribute the funds and has handed them over to the Relief Committees of your provinces for distribution. We hereby inform you by telegram. The Shanghai Fundraising Emergency Relief Association for Flood Disasters in Various Provinces kowtows. In addition, the Anhui Compatriots Emergency Relief Association in Tianjin has previously raised 10,000 yuan for relief funds and remitted them to Shanghai to be distributed by Xu Shiying for emergency relief in the four counties of WuShou, Fengtai, and YingShang in northern Anhui. Xu Shiying has dispatched relief committee member Xu Guoyuan, accompanied by relief friends Li Qinlian and Zhou Xue 税, to carry the funds to Bengbu, convene representatives from the four counties, and distribute them in separate ways on the same day, and has telegraphed Shanghai and Tianjin to report.

Establishment of the Disaster Victim Shelter Office 120

Since the establishment of the office by uniting various sectors in this city to accommodate disaster victims, preparations have been actively made, and it has officially been established and started working yesterday. The first shelter in Liuying Road will be completed on the 4th and can accommodate more than 4,000 people. The various situations are recorded in detail below:

▲ Official Establishment

The Disaster Victim Shelter Office in this city was officially established yesterday morning at 9:00 AM at 293 Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen, Nanshi. More than 30 people attended, including Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Feng Liutang, Section Chief, Wu Liguo, Section Chief of the Health Bureau, Shen 　, Shen Zengfu of the Public Security Bureau, Wang Yiting, Ye Huijun, and Sun Yishan. There was no opening ceremony.

▲ Announcement to All Sectors

The Disaster Victim Shelter Office in this city announced to all sectors yesterday, stating that this year's floods in various provinces have been massive, and disaster victims have been arriving in Shanghai one after another, urgently needing accommodation. The office has now borrowed the Gugong Institute at 639 Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen, Nanshi, for office space and is officially established on September 1. Land has been found to accommodate the disaster victims. In addition to reporting to the municipal government for record-keeping, notices have been sent to various agencies, organizations, and newspapers for reference. (Telephone Nanshi 126, Chinese and foreign registered). Furthermore, this office does not send people to solicit donations outside. However, the disaster victims arriving in Shanghai are incompletely clothed and look haggard. The autumn wind is harsh, and the cold dew is chilling. If people from all walks of life are willing to donate food, clothing, and daily necessities, regardless of size or newness, as long as they do not compromise hygiene, they will be benefiting the disaster victims, and we will gratefully receive and distribute them on their behalf. As for disaster relief agencies and organizations, if they are willing to allocate funds to subsidize the shelter's expenses, please send them directly to this office, and receipts will be issued. At the end of the operation, the income and expenditure will be published in the newspaper to show good faith. This announcement is made by Wang Zhen, Director of the Shanghai Disaster Victim Shelter Office, and Deputy Directors Ye Huijun, Chen Xizeng, Hu Hongji, and Pan Gongzhan.

▲ Service Meeting

The first service meeting was held at the City Disaster Victim Shelter Office at 10:00 AM yesterday. Feng Liutang, Wu Liguo, Shen Zengfu, Shen Guansheng, Sun Shan, and other directors and deputy directors of the General Affairs, Health, Security, and Logistics Sections attended. Wang Yiting chaired the meeting and reported on the progress of accommodating the disaster victims. The meeting then discussed the operation of the office and the logistics issues in detail. Each section immediately began working.

▲ Clothing for Disaster Relief

The Disaster Victim Shelter Office in this city received the following yesterday: (1) Ms. Zhang, residing at 113 Kongjia Street, Laoximen, donated 29 pieces of clothing, including 3 large and 13 small single garments, 10 large and small lined garments, and 3 large and small cotton garments; (2) Ding Huiji, residing at Yingbing Inn, Dada Li, 16th Pier, donated 12 pieces of clothing, including 9 large and small single garments, 2 small lined garments, and 2 cotton garments. All were personally delivered.

▲ Arrangement in the Shelter

The first shelter of the City Disaster Victim Shelter Office, located at the old camp base on Liuying Road, Zhabei, has been under construction by the Public Works Bureau since the 30th and has been partially completed. It is scheduled to be fully completed on the 4th and can accommodate more than 4,000 disaster victims. After completion, more than 1,000 disaster victims who have already been accommodated will be moved in. The internal equipment is very complete. There are 400 disaster victim rooms, 2 male and 2 female bathrooms with shower equipment, 1 fire station with a fire truck stationed by Zhabei, 2 security rooms with police stationed by the Public Security Bureau, 1 office for administrators, 2 storage rooms, 1 peace room, 1 water kitchen, 1 kitchen, and 1 temporary hospital (i.e., sanatorium) with 8 rooms for patients and 2 rooms for clinics. The construction cost is 15,000 yuan. The floorboards are all provided by the members of the Construction Industry Association. Tap water has been installed by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company.

▲ Personal Inspection

At 1:00 PM yesterday, Feng Liutang, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, Mo Heng, Section Chief of the Public Works Bureau, and Wu Liguo, Section Chief of the Health Bureau, personally went to the first shelter of the City Disaster Victim Shelter Office on Liuying Road, Zhabei, to inspect the construction project and returned at 4:00 PM. The disaster victims in Shanghai are issued 20 cents per day per person for large rations and 10 cents for small rations.

Another Batch of Refugees Arrived Yesterday 121

In recent days, many refugees from provinces such as Jiangxi and Hubei have been brought in by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jianghua, Jiangda, and Jianguo ships. At 2:30 PM yesterday, another approximately 500 to 600 refugees from the three provinces of Jiangxi, Hubei, and Anhui were brought in by the company's Jiangxin ship. After the ship docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf, more than 200 people went to visit relatives on their own. Those who had no relatives to rely on, after disembarking, raised the refugee flag and were led by officials from the Disaster Victim Shelter Office to the guild halls in the Xieqiao and Rihui Port area for accommodation.

Xinghua Disaster Victims Describe the Tragedy 122

After the breaches of the embankments in the Gaoyou and Shaobo areas, the water level of the canal dropped sharply by five or six feet, rushing straight down to the lower reaches like a collapsing building. Xinghua, which is located at the bottom, suffered the most. Yesterday, some disaster victims from the county escaped to Shanghai. According to them, the water volume in the county has increased by another four feet. Villages within hundreds of miles around have been completely submerged. The treetops and the roofs of houses that were slightly above the water surface a few days ago have also been almost completely submerged. Young and strong people climb trees to wait for rescue, and most of the women and children have drowned. The entire city is flooded, and the county government, which is the highest point, is also three feet deep in water. In other low-lying areas, the water is higher than the eaves. Houses collapsing are heard every day. Dozens of sections of the city walls have been destroyed by the water, and the water and sky are connected outside the city. Cooking smoke has long ceased. People are continuing their lives in boats, not knowing what tomorrow will bring. All the remaining food has also been washed away and cannot be eaten anymore. The entire area is experiencing dangerous winds and waves, and transportation is blocked. The northern area, such as Zhongbao Ganggu, is particularly low-lying, and the water depth is estimated to be two zhang. Hundreds of thousands of households in that area may have already been buried in the bellies of fish. It is said that if the breaches in the canal embankments are not blocked early, the disaster situation in the county will never be alleviated.

NingShao Emergency Relief Association Meeting Today 123

The NingShao Emergency Relief Association for the Hankou Disaster delivered 60 boxes of biscuits that had been prepared yesterday, a large item of Thunderstrike Powder (donated by the Morality Association), and 500 bags of flour and 71 boxes of bread entrusted by the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association to the Yihua Company's Longhe ship for shipment to Hankou for distribution. It was also reported that the association received a telegram from Yin Huichang, the representative stationed in Hankou to handle relief efforts, requesting assistance from Hankou compatriots in setting up an epidemic prevention hospital. The relief team previously sent to Hankou escorted the disaster-stricken compatriots to Ningbo on the Yongxing ship on the 31st. The magistrate of Yin County, Chen Baolin, telegraphed that they were expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning to report on the situation. It has been decided that a meeting of all committee members will be convened at 4:00 PM on the 2nd of this month to discuss the matter.
