Sichuan Fellow Villagers Association Telegraphs National Government for Disaster Relief 126

The Sichuan Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai yesterday submitted a report to the National Government detailing the severe flooding in Sichuan Province. The report requested a large sum of money be allocated swiftly for disaster relief and that the Sichuan military forces be ordered to abolish exorbitant taxes levied in advance to alleviate the people's suffering. According to telegrams from various Sichuan people's organizations and representatives of the Sichuan Flood Relief Association in Shanghai, torrential rains began in Sichuan Province between July and August, causing the Tuo River, Min River, and Bei River basins to flood simultaneously. Other counties also experienced sudden mountain floods. The northern Sichuan region was relatively lightly affected, with only Santai, Suining, Yingshan, and other counties suffering the drowning of livestock, farmland, and houses, resulting in losses of tens of thousands in each. While the counties along the Fu River also suffered damage, it was not as severe as the aforementioned. In southern Sichuan, counties such as Rongjing, Weiyuan, Leshan, Gulin, and Yunlian in Shangnan were inundated by mountain floods, with water levels so high that one could wash their feet on top of the city walls. Houses and farmland were largely swept away, and the number of disaster victims reached more than half of the population in each of these counties. Ziyang, Zizhong, Neijiang, Fushun, Luzhou, Hejiang, and Yibin in Xianan, especially the first four counties, were almost entirely submerged by the Tuo River. Along the river for hundreds of miles, the water was seven to eight zhang (approximately 21 to 24 meters) high above ground level, drowning more than 10,000 people and submerging more than ten towns. The farmland and houses destroyed were beyond counting. The latter three counties, located in critical areas of the Min River, had both their urban and rural areas turned into swamps where boats could travel. The situation in Luzhou and Hejiang was particularly dire. In eastern Sichuan, Rongchang, Chongqing, Jiangbei Hechuan, Jiangjin in Shangdong and Wanxian, Kaixian, Fuling, Xiushan, Pengshui in Xiadong suffered flooding. Rongchang, Xiushan, and Pengshui were submerged by mountain floods, while the others were affected by the Yangtze River. According to the customs waterway reports, the Yangtze River flood reached a height of twelve zhang and several chi (approximately 36 to 39 meters), so the damage to humans, livestock, and houses can be imagined. Many families were completely wiped out, and entire villages were in ruins. In western Sichuan, areas from Beichuan, Anxian, Mianyang, and Maogong in the north to Chengdu, Jintang, and Jianyang in the south were flooded by rivers or streams. The ferocity of the floods was unprecedented in the past century. After the disaster, the price of rice soared to sixty or seventy yuan per shi (approximately 50 kg). Starving people were everywhere, and instances of cannibalism among the old and young occurred, highlighting the tragedy of human existence. In total, more than ninety counties in Sichuan Province were affected by the floods, with more than thirty of them severely affected. It is estimated that there are over one million helpless disaster victims. Although Chengdu and Chongqing have taken measures to provide relief, it is merely a drop in the bucket and does little to address the situation. The report requests the Association to raise funds for relief efforts and appeal to the central government. Upon hearing this, the Association was heartbroken. In addition to gathering the Sichuanese in Shanghai to raise funds and appealing to various charitable organizations for joint rescue efforts as an urgent measure, the Association noted that since spring, Sichuan Province has been experiencing drought conditions, and calls for grain relief have been widespread throughout the region. Now, the province has been hit by severe flooding, which has not only destroyed existing properties but also swept away the crops that were about to be harvested and the farmlands that were relied upon for survival. As the saying goes, "a house as empty as a bell," but now even the house is gone. As the saying goes, "not sure of tomorrow," but now not even sure of the morning. Given this situation, it is impossible to survive the year, let alone the day. Although the government Relief Committee allocated 10,000 yuan for emergency relief, this only amounts to one fen (one-hundredth of a yuan) per person for the million disaster victims, which is hardly enough to solve the urgent problem. The local authorities in Sichuan have also proposed relief measures, but they are essentially taking from the left hand to heal the right, which the people dare not accept. After repeated consideration, the Association earnestly requests the government to promptly order the Relief Committee and the Flood Relief Committee to consider the severity of the disaster in Sichuan, allocate more relief funds to Sichuan, or directly send personnel to the affected areas to provide relief, in order to save millions of disaster victims from death. This is the first request. The military warlords in Sichuan are notorious for exploiting the people through various means. For example, if one army has a bullet fee, another army will have a uniform fee, and a third army will have a straw sandal fee. They invent various pretexts to demand money from the people without any regard. As for the Likin tax, which the central government has explicitly abolished, they not only refuse to abolish it but also set up checkpoints everywhere, appearing several times in one li (approximately 500 meters). As for the advance levies, which the central government has explicitly prohibited, some collect taxes in advance until the 40s of the Republic era, and some require people to pay grain taxes monthly. The Anti-Opium Investigation Bureaus, which the central government has abolished, have been operating for years with remarkable results. There are also compulsory seedling donations, lazy donations, and monopoly fees for scales, inspection fees, and lamp and license fees. Under these harsh levies, how can the people not be impoverished? Now that the impoverished are further impoverished by floods, they cannot bear any more levies. Therefore, the Association cannot help but earnestly request the government to strictly order the military forces in Sichuan not to levy any more exorbitant taxes in order to save the remaining lives of the people. If they dare to disobey, the people should be allowed to file charges. This is the second request. All of the above reasons are hereby submitted to the government for review, verification, and instruction. Respectfully submitted to the National Government.

Meeting Minutes of the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association 127

The French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association convened a meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee yesterday at 3 PM to discuss ways to provide relief to the provinces affected by flooding. The attendees included Shang Mujiang, Zhu Shengmao, Xie Qianggong, Dong Kechang, Xu Xiuting, Shen Zhongjun, Cheng Zhusun, Tao Leqin, Tong Lizhang, Li Weiliang, Xu Caicheng, Qu Zhenhua, and others, totaling twelve members. Shang Mujiang was elected as the chairman of the meeting. The following matters were discussed: (1) To facilitate the raising of relief supplies, a disaster relief committee will be formed within the Association. (2) According to a letter from Mr. Xu Langxi, the disaster areas are expanding daily, and the weather is getting colder. While the issue of food is important, the issue of clothing is even more important. Therefore, the Association will focus on collecting clothing and will not accept cash. The collected clothing will be transferred to the disaster relief committee for distribution. (3) Arrangements have been made with the Shandong Guildhall to serve as the committee's office. (4) A letter will be sent to various organizations informing them of the Association's plan to form a committee to collect old cotton padded jackets, trousers, and other items. (5) To expand publicity, in addition to publishing advertisements, printing illustrations, declarations, and leaflets, all members of the Association must be responsible for publicity at all times and solicit donations everywhere. (6) The committee's expenses are limited to 300 to 500 yuan. (7) A report on the clothing and other items collected will be submitted by the Association every ten days. Zhu Shengmao and Lou Hongjun were appointed as organizers. (8) Shang Mujiang was appointed to oversee illustrations, Xie Qianggong to oversee writing, Tong Lizhang to oversee publicity, Zhu Shengmao and Li Weiliang to oversee printing, and Cheng Zhusun to oversee finance. (9) All executive supervisory committee members of the Association will attend meetings every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday from 3 PM to 4 PM to handle all relevant matters. (10) The chairman reported on letters received from various parties and the Association's letter to the French Police, requesting that they inform their officers not to misunderstand the Association's posting of disaster relief leaflets. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Meeting Minutes of the Jiangxi Emergency Relief Association 128

The Shanghai Jiangxi Emergency Relief Association held its eighth regular committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 4 PM. The attendees included Zhang Yuejun, Wen Lanting, Wang Peiyuan, Yu Qiaqing, Xiong Shihui's representative, Tang Yi, and others. Wen Lanting was elected as the chairman. Tang Yi reported on the recent situation of banditry and flooding in Jiangxi, as well as the relief efforts. He also conveyed Commander Xiong's hope that Shanghai would send additional relief workers to assist in supervision and promotion. After discussion, it was resolved to issue the following announcement in the name of the Association's Presidium: Since its establishment, the Association has been operating within the Red Cross for several months. Thanks to the generous support of philanthropists from all walks of life, significant achievements have been made. Recently, due to the urgent need for relief in various provinces affected by flooding, the Association's fundraising efforts have been temporarily suspended, which is regrettable. It has been found that the destruction caused by banditry in 43 counties in Jiangxi is even worse than that caused by flooding. The plan for providing relief to the bandit-affected areas is currently being designed by the Party and Government Committee, and General Commander Chiang Kai-shek is also making great efforts to ensure its success. It is a matter of national livelihood and the safety of the nation. The Association, having already made meager contributions as a support, should continue to work hard to achieve its original goal. Therefore, the regular committee has unanimously resolved that, starting from September 1st, it will resume normal operations within the Red Cross. It is hoped that all colleagues in the Association and benefactors from all walks of life will work together to achieve this goal.

Wheat Seed Issues in the Floods 134

Opinions of Dr. Love of the United States

American Wheat is Unsuitable for Chinese Soil

Mis-planting American Wheat will be Inconceivable

Should Collect Existing Wheat Seeds Quickly

This year's floods in various provinces not only mean that most of the autumn harvest is hopeless, but the problem of wheat seeds will also cause panic, especially in the areas most affected by the floods. Because disaster victims lack food, most of the wheat seeds left are used for food. Therefore, after the flood recedes, wheat seeds will inevitably be scarce. It is now heard that the plan to provide relief to the flood victims will involve shipping a large amount of American wheat to China for use as food in the disaster areas. This is very good, but it is also suggested that American wheat, in addition to being used for food, should also be used for planting. According to Dr. Love, an agricultural advisor to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Chief Technician for Crop Improvement in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, American wheat is definitely not suitable for Chinese soil, especially in the areas most affected by floods in the Yangtze River basin, where the climate and soil are even more unsuitable. If American wheat is mistakenly used for planting, the consequences will be inconceivable and will inevitably cause an even greater panic about food next year. It is hoped that the organizations or personnel responsible for distributing American wheat to farmers in the future must earnestly guide the farmers to use it only for food and not to keep it for planting. Regarding the method of remedying the wheat seed shortage this year, it is hoped that the flood relief committee can promptly collect the wheat that still exists in the Yangtze River basin and exchange it for other food or money. After the flood recedes, the collected wheat seeds will be distributed to farmers for planting. This is the most important thing at the moment. A slight delay will result in countless wheat seeds being used by farmers to satisfy their hunger.

The main text of the judgment reads: Xie Fuxiang, Wan Haiqing, Zhang Ronghui, and Wu Liaoqing are each sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for jointly committing robbery in a group of three or more people. Fu Quan is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for protecting stolen goods. Yang Minggao is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for hiding stolen goods. Yang Weimin, Xu Mingsheng, and Li Binyuan are each sentenced to six months of imprisonment for receiving stolen goods. The number of days of detention shall be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two days. Meng Linchun, Yan Menglin, and Wang Fushi are found not guilty. The criminal proceedings against Ma Zhicheng are suspended. The recovered marked banknotes are confiscated and deposited in the post office. The clothes purchased with the stolen money are returned to the Traffic Commercial Trust Company for collection. The unmarked banknotes and the 300 yuan deposit slip are confiscated and deposited in the police station, pending a civil lawsuit by the plaintiff.

Continued Hearing Postponed

Guohua Electric Company, located at 418 Gongguan Road in the French Concession, was reported to the Ministry of Transportation by the International Telecommunications Bureau for disrupting international telecommunications and violating the telecommunications regulations by installing a wireless broadcasting station. Chinese and Western detectives, together with Xu Zhuoyun, an official from the International Telecommunications Bureau, went to Guohua Electric Company to search and seized the equipment used for the wireless broadcasting station. The defendant hired Yan Xuanzhendong as his lawyer to defend him. Because Zhao Xudong, the manager of Guohua, did not appear in court, the hearing was postponed. The details have been recorded in the previous report. According to the manager of Guohua Electric Company, Guohua installed the wireless broadcasting station to develop its business and entertain the audience, broadcasting records, storytelling, and other programs every day, without any inappropriate behavior. On the 14th of last month, the company received a notice from the French Police Department to stop broadcasting and immediately dismantled the station. On the 19th, the company received another letter from the French Municipal Council stating that Guohua's radio waves were disrupting the telecommunications of neighboring radio stations and that broadcasting should be stopped immediately, otherwise a public prosecution would be filed. At that time, the broadcasting equipment had already been dismantled and stored in the warehouse. Xu Zhuoyun, an official from the International Telecommunications Bureau, together with police detectives, came to search on the afternoon of the 21st. When asked by the shop assistants, they replied that it had already been dismantled. Because the visitors did not believe them, they searched the broadcasting room and later seized the equipment used for the broadcasting station in the warehouse and took it away. The original hearing of the case was scheduled for yesterday morning. Zhao Xudong, the manager of Guohua Electric Company, and his lawyer appeared in court to await instructions. Because the procedures for the case were not yet complete, the continued hearing was postponed.

Pig Boat Overturned by Wind 141

Four Crew Members Drowned

The pig boat Chen Changxing from Jiangbei, this time loaded with 157 live pigs from Renjiagang, was sailing to Shanghai, intending to meet the market demand for the Ghost Festival in the seventh lunar month. Unexpectedly, at the end of last month, while passing near Liuhe, it encountered a sudden gale that broke the mast and sails. The boat drifted to the front of the Wusong Lion Grove Fort, where it ran aground on a hidden sandbar and capsized. All eight crew members and pig merchants, along with the live pigs, fell into the water. Four crew members, including Xu Er, Lu Da, and Zhang Waizui, drowned. The remaining four, pig merchant Liu Tong and crew members Zhang Tai, Du Gehuan, and Bao Peipei, managed to climb onto the ship's planks and drifted with the waves. Soldiers on watch at the fort spotted them and immediately reported to Commander Shi Ze, who dispatched six soldiers in a boat to rescue them. They were fortunate to be saved. The pig merchant and crew members then devised a plan to use the anchor chains of the overturned boat to secure it to the seawall south of the fort. They immediately telegraphed the pig boat owner, Chen Hengde. However, it was discovered that the iron anchor chain of the boat had been stolen the night before. The boat then drifted with the tide to Songkou, where it was discovered by the Fourth Squad of the Water Police. Yesterday, boat owner Chen arrived in Song, learned of the situation, and immediately reported it to the Fourth Squad, requesting that the thief of the anchor be apprehended and prosecuted.

Xu Mengxiang Seriously Injured

The injured were taken by family members to Baolong Hospital for treatment. Filial Son Savagely Beats His Elderly Mother 145

Gao Wubao Devoid of Conscience

Gao Qi's Life Hanging by a Thread

Gao Qi, an elderly woman from Tongzhou, is 78 years old and lives at No. 4, Lane 74, Xiaoputuo Bridge Street, outside Xiaonanmen in the Nanshi district. She has two sons. The elder, Gao Wubao, is 40 years old and works as a peddler. However, Wubao is addicted to gambling and has squandered all his meager earnings on gambling, both day and night. Over time, all the family's belongings have been pawned or sold. He has repeatedly borrowed from relatives and friends to no end, and is too embarrassed to borrow again, leaving him nearly destitute. He has long neglected his mother's livelihood. Fortunately, her younger son is able to provide for her. However, Wubao still frequently asks his mother and brother for money. Yesterday morning at around 10:00 AM, Wubao came home again and asked his sister-in-law, Wang, for a loan. Wang refused politely, as she had no money. However, Wubao cursed her. He then begged his mother for money, but she also refused. At this point, Wubao became enraged and immediately rushed into the bedroom, destroying his mother's bed and cursing her loudly. Qi became extremely angry upon hearing this and scolded him slightly. Wubao immediately lunged at her, grabbed her, and savagely beat her. Qi was old and weak and unable to resist, resulting in injuries all over her body and causing her to collapse to the ground, barely breathing. Gong Rongsheng, the watchman of the Eleventh Post in the area, heard the commotion and rushed over, immediately arresting the unfilial son Gao Wubao and taking him and his mother to the First Precinct, First Station. After a preliminary hearing by the station chief, he was found to have abused his parent, displaying a beastly nature. He was ordered to prepare a document for submission to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Records of the Pilotage Rights Case 147

Selection Set for October 1st

28 Qualified Chinese Candidates

The Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Navy, and the Ministry of Communications advocated the recovery of foreign pilotage rights, the establishment of a management committee, and the holding of examinations to implement the transfer of pilotage rights and gradually reduce the number of foreign pilots. This matter has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the pilotage examination for all seaports has been centrally decided to take place in Shanghai on October 1st, with the Ministry of Navy responsible for the administration. The Ministry of Navy submitted a report to the Executive Yuan regarding the recovery of pilotage, outlining the reasons for China's loss of rights. It stated that seaport pilotage is the guide to a nation's gateway. All countries in the East and West have exclusive pilotage services for their own people, emphasizing the sovereignty of territory and people. Since China opened its ports to trade, most of the pilots at various ports have been foreigners. During the Sino-French War of 1884, French warships suddenly penetrated deep into the Min River, guided by an American pilot. The Chinese navy was unable to respond to this extraordinary event, resulting in a loss of troops. It was a painful lesson. At the time, the Qing government questioned the US government and requested that the American pilot be punished. The US Secretary of State replied that if there were a war between the US and France, an American pilot guiding an enemy of the US into US territory would be punished by law. Since this case, China has allowed Americans to serve as pilots in the Min River. During the Sino-French War, an American guided French warships into Chinese territory, but even though the pilot was captured, the US side did not punish him because there was no legal basis. Therefore, the employment of foreigners as pilots in China's seaports not only hinders sovereignty but also makes it difficult to cope in wartime and during periods of martial law, according to Article 3 of the martial law regulations. A fundamental solution should be sought to abolish foreign pilots. However, seaport pilotage is related to the safety of foreign warships entering the ports, and pilots must be proficient in navigation technology. For the sake of overall planning and preventing foreign threats, in addition to establishing a pilot training institute to reserve talent, the Ministry also collaborated with the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Communications to draft pilotage management and examination regulations, totaling nine chapters and fifty-one articles, which were submitted for promulgation. The regulations stipulate the establishment of a management committee to place pilotage entirely under government control, so that more Chinese people can serve as pilots, the number of foreign pilots can be reduced day by day, and the goal of having all domestic seaport pilotage affairs entirely under the control of the Chinese people can be realized as soon as possible.

This pilotage examination is scheduled for October 1st at the Ministry of Navy's Pilotage Training Institute. There are 28 qualified candidates in China, all maritime professionals from the Shanghai Drivers' Association who have served as ship owners. It is reported that the Ministry of Navy, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Communications have stipulated the following qualifications for pilotage examination: (1) Citizen of the Republic of China; (2) Possess a certificate from a specialized school of navigation; (3) Have a proven record of service in the designated pilotage area; (4) Possess good character, sound health, and no addictions. The examination emphasizes vision, requiring 6/6 and 9/9 acuity and the ability to distinguish colors without error. Hearing must be able to distinguish ordinary conversation at a distance of six meters and be able to use the compass to change direction and determine the direction of travel. Candidates must be familiar with all navigation facilities and other maritime skills in the pilotage area.

The Shanghai Pilotage Association strongly advocates that foreigners no longer participate in pilotage. The Ministry of Navy has replied, stating that the Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Communications stipulated in the "Provisional Measures for Pilotage in Various Chinese Ports" in March of this year that seaport pilotage should be managed by the Customs. The Ministry objected to this regulation based on the principle of pilotage sovereignty and submitted a report to the Executive Yuan. The pilotage examination regulations were promulgated and implemented on May 3 of this year, and the examination has been scheduled. Since there are established laws to follow, there is no need to worry. As it concerns maritime defense, it should be carried out properly to appease the public.

Complete Suspension of Chinese Merchant Steamships 148

British Merchants Thriving

▲ Sanbei Line Completely Suspended: The Yangtze River ships of the Sanbei Company in Shanghai had excellent business after the boycott of Japanese goods. As a result, the Yangtze River routes in Shanghai have been completely suspended. However, to meet the needs of passengers, shallow-water ships from the upper Yangtze River will be transferred to maintain some traffic.

▲ China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Suspends Sailings: Due to the recent floods in Hankou, the wharves and warehouses of all companies were submerged, except for those of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which were protected by levees built by Li Yunliang. Not only were passengers and cargo preserved from major damage, but the company also gained the favor of customers and enjoyed thriving business. However, due to urgent transportation needs, the Jiang'an, Jianghua, Jianguo, Jiangda, Jiangtian, Jiangyu, Kuaili, and Emei were sent to Jiujiang after unloading disaster victims in Shanghai. The Xiaochangjiang ships of Dada and Datong have also each sent one or two ships to Xun for duty.

▲ Rise of British Merchant Ships: Since the boycott, Chinese goods have been diverted from Japanese ships. With the recent suspension of Chinese Yangtze River ships, the Yangtze River business of Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson has greatly increased. The business of Heba Company has also been incorporated into these two companies, naturally increasing the volume of imports and exports. Jardine Matheson will take the opportunity to launch a special Shanghai-Changsha-Yichang express service every Wednesday and Saturday, starting this Wednesday.

Measures for the First Land Reclamation in the Central District 149

Measures for Party and Government Agency Staff to Acquire Land Also Decided

The Shanghai Municipal Government's 189th Municipal Conference resolved the measures for the second land reclamation in the central area of Shanghai. Excerpts are as follows: (1) The reclamation area is defined as the land north of Sanmin Road, southeast of Zhanyin Road, southwest of the planned trunk road, and northwest of the administrative district (map omitted). (2) Land prices are divided into two types: 2,000 yuan and 2,500 yuan per mu. (3) Each household is limited to reclaiming one to four mu of land. (4) The start date for registration will be announced by the Land Bureau. (5) One month before the start of registration, the original landowners have priority to apply for the return of their land. Within 15 days after the start of registration, those reclaiming one mu of land can apply for registration with the Land Bureau and pay a deposit of 500 yuan per mu. (6) After the registration deadline for those reclaiming one mu of land, the Land Bureau will set a date to notify them to draw lots. Those who draw a lot for a certain district and number will receive land in that district and number. (7) After the registration of those reclaiming one mu of land, the Land Bureau will continue to process the registration of those reclaiming two mu or more of land. The registration and lottery dates will be announced separately. The land reclamation method is the same as for those reclaiming one mu of land. (8) If the land reclaimed under this item is within the designated commercial or residential area, all buildings should be compatible with the regulations of each area. (9) The building area in the commercial area shall not be less than two-tenths of the total area of the reclaimed land, and the building area in the residential area shall not be less than one-tenth of the total area of the reclaimed land. (10) Houses built in this reclamation area, whether shops or residences, are exempt from house tax for three years, calculated from the date of the start of land reclamation. (11) When the land reclaimed under this item is resold to others, it is exempt from transfer tax for five years, calculated from the date of issuance of the land license.

In addition, the measures for staff of the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee and the various bureaus affiliated with the Municipal Government to acquire land in the central area of the city have also been resolved as follows: (1) The area for acquisition is defined as the land north of Xiangyin Road, southeast of the administrative district, and south and west of the park area (map omitted). (2) Staff of the Municipal Party Committee and the various bureaus of the Municipal Government who enjoy the right to acquire land in the central area of the city are limited to those whose offices are located in the central administrative district and who must reside in the central area of the city. (3) Staff members shall not acquire land in the name of others. If it is found that there is such a substitution, in addition to canceling the land acquisition, the deposit and land price paid shall be confiscated. (4) Each person is limited to acquiring a maximum of two mu of land. Those who acquire less than one mu should combine with other staff members to acquire a whole mu. (5) Land prices are divided into two types: 2,000 yuan and 2,500 yuan per mu. (6) The Municipal Party Committee and the various bureaus of the Municipal Government shall first send a list of those acquiring land to the Land Bureau, and then the land acquirers shall apply for registration with the Land Bureau and pay the deposit according to the regulations. The deposit is temporarily set at 500 yuan per mu. (7) One month before the start of registration is the priority period for the original landowners to apply for the return of their land. (8) After the registration deadline, the Land Bureau will notify the acquirers to draw lots according to the registration number. (9) Houses built in this land acquisition area are exempt from house tax for three years, calculated from the date of the start of land acquisition. (10) The area of houses built in this land acquisition area shall not be less than one-tenth of the total area of the land acquired. (11) Staff members who acquire land must reside there themselves. Before paying off the land price and building houses, the land shall not be transferred. (12) When the land acquired under this item is resold to others, it is exempt from transfer tax for five years, calculated from the date of issuance of the land license.

Silk Factories Gradually Recover 150

Situation After the Issuance of Public Bonds

Of the 106 silk factories in Shanghai, this spring, due to the poor sales of foreign silk, they suffered a severe setback, and their funds were completely depleted. They reduced the number of machines and stopped work one after another. After the new cocoons were released on the market, there was still no improvement in European sales. Only 36 silk factories in the city were barely able to start work. Now, because 4 million of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds have been issued since the 31st, silk merchants in Zhejiang and Wuxi have each obtained certificates signed and sealed by Qian Fenghao and Chu Huiseng, the chairmen of the silk factory trade associations in their respective areas, to claim the bond coupons they are entitled to from the Trust Department of the Shanghai Guohuo Bank (the commissioned issuer of the silk public bond fund). About 50-60% of the local manufacturers in this city have gone to apply for the bonds. The factories that have stopped work are now preparing to start work. The 36 silk factories that have started work previously reduced their work to half-days during the summer vacation. Now that autumn has arrived, they have all resumed full-day work yesterday. By around the 15th of this month, it is expected that 60-70% of the silk factories in Shanghai will have resumed operations.

The Unified Tax Bureau Announces That Goods Must Have Stamps Affixed After Tax Payment 151

Otherwise, the Tax Owed Will Be Collected

The Unified Tax Bureau announced: In order to announce matters, it is found that the unified tax on imported cigarettes, cotton yarn, wheat flour, matches, and cement has been collected by the Customs. After paying the tax, merchants should take the second copy of the unified tax receipt, together with the original yellow declaration form signed by the customs officer, to this bureau or the local unified tax bureau office to submit it for verification, request personnel to supervise the affixing of stamps or fill out a tax ticket transportation permit, so that the goods can be shipped out and sold. The first copy of the unified tax form will be sent by the Customs to this bureau or the local unified tax agency at any time, and the amount of tax collected will be entered into the account for verification. This is a prescribed procedure and has long been implemented and complied with. However, it has been found recently that when marketing goods in the Shanghai area, merchants often do not comply with the prescribed procedures after paying the unified tax to the Customs, and they do not submit the second copy of the unified tax form held to the bureau for verification, request stamps, or clear the tax permit procedures, making it extremely difficult to verify and clear accounts in this bureau's books. Since this situation exists in Shanghai, it is feared that the provinces will also be unavoidable. This kind of violation of the regulations, arbitrarily delayed for a long time, should be clearly announced regarding the original restrictions on the period for requesting tax permits set by the former resident customs office, in order to comply with it. It is found that imported tobacco items from foreign countries in the past, after merchants paid taxes, should apply for stamps on the same day according to regulations. If the time limit is exceeded and the stamps are not reported, the stamps for that time, together with the tax receipt, will be invalid. This case has been stipulated for a long time and should be repeatedly warned and continue to be followed. Hereafter, after merchants pay the unified tax on the aforementioned imported goods, they should bring the second copy of the tax form to this bureau or the local unified tax bureau office within two weeks to report and request to exchange it for a stamp permit. Those with special circumstances who are unable to apply within the time limit are allowed to report in advance from the date of payment, with a deadline of one month at the latest, and no further extension will be allowed for the convenience of merchants. If the time limit is exceeded and the flower license is still not exchanged in accordance with the regulations, the original unified tax form should be invalidated. In the future, when goods are shipped or sold, the tax owed must be paid separately before the flower license can be issued to warn against fatigue and delay, and to show the restrictions. In addition to general circulation, this notice is issued to urge all merchants to comply. All goods that have not been exchanged for flower licenses should quickly bring the second copy of the tax form to report and receive stamps, or request to fill in a tax permit. Hereafter, all must comply with the time limit and not exceed the deadline and delay themselves, leading to supplementary tax payment.

Heavy Taxes Levied on Goods Transported to Guangdong 153

The Ministry of Finance Notifies That Those Who Have Paid the Unified Tax Will Be Refunded

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday: We have received your telegram regarding the case of goods transported to Guangdong being subject to duplicate taxation. According to the principles of the unified tax, after goods are taxed and leave the factory, they can be transported freely without being subject to any further taxes or levies. However, since the political change in Guangdong Province, all goods that have been taxed in Shanghai and other places are being subject to heavy taxation when they arrive in Guangdong. In order to maintain the spirit of the unified tax and avoid merchants bearing double taxation, the Ministry has approved that for goods that have been subject to heavy taxation in Guangdong Province, merchants can present evidence and request the Unified Tax Bureau to refund the original taxes paid in Shanghai and other places. Therefore, goods transported from Shanghai and other places to Guangdong have not been taxed by this Ministry. If they are transported back to Shanghai or other unified tax areas from Guangdong Province, the tax owed must be paid. This is the way it is done everywhere. How can Zhao'an's port be any different? As for the taxes paid by merchants at Zhao'an's port, they can still refer to the precedent of the Unified Tax Bureau for tax refunds, present evidence, and request a refund from the Guangdong Provincial Tax Bureau. There is no loss to the merchants. The Zhao'an Chamber of Commerce has already presented this matter directly, and a reply has been issued tomorrow. Please investigate and comply.

The Organization of Fellow-Native Associations 158

Should Be Based on the Revised Organizational Plan for People's Associations

The organization of fellow-native associations should be handled in accordance with the currently revised organizational plan for people's associations. The Executive Committee of this city previously sent lawyer Huang Boshang to inquire, and a reply has been received as follows: (Respectfully, Upon reviewing the files taken over, regarding your lawyer's letter of July 25th inquiring whether the organization of fellow-native associations should follow the organizational procedures for vocational associations and requesting instructions, etc., we hereby reply that when the Organizational Plan for People's Associations was originally promulgated by the central government, it focused on vocational associations and was brief on social associations. However, at the same time, organizational procedures for social associations were promulgated and implemented to supplement the inadequacies of the plan. Now, the aforementioned organizational plan has been carefully revised and re-promulgated by the central government, and its content is suitable for various vocational and social associations without discrimination. The previously promulgated organizational procedures for social associations have also been abolished simultaneously. Therefore, the organization of all fellow-native associations, etc., should be handled in accordance with the methods prescribed in the currently revised Organizational Plan for People's Associations. The letter is hereby replied. Accordingly, we enclose one copy each of the revised Organizational Plan for People's Associations and the Matters That Should Be Stipulated and Specified in the Articles of Association of Charitable Organizations for your reference. Sincerely,)

Inspection Report of the Central Bank 160

100th Time

The 100th inspection report of the Central Bank's issuance reserves states: "This association, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the issuance of convertible banknotes of the bank. The 100th inspection was held on August 31, 1931, at the bank's issuing bureau. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible banknotes issued: 37,591,858 silver dollars, including 34,869,751 silver dollar banknotes and 2,722,107 subsidiary currency banknotes. Total amount of convertible banknote reserves: 37,591,858 silver dollars, including 24,586,146 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 15,595,914.61 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 3,950,338 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 5,039,893.39 silver dollars deposited with fellow banks. The guarantee reserve converted to silver dollars is 13,005,712 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold convertible banknotes issued: 1,000,000 customs gold units. Total amount of customs gold convertible banknote reserves: 1,000,000 customs gold units. This reserve includes US$400,000 deposited with fellow banks in this city, converted to customs gold at a fixed rate of 40. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeded 60%, while the guarantee reserve was less than 40%. This is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. August 31, 1931. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun; Supervisors, Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Ji."

Two Female Workers Gone Without a Trace 163

Two Taixing People Are Suspected

Li Wanxi, a native of Yancheng residing in the workshop of the Shanghai Third Cotton Mill on Pingliang Road, his wife Zhang, 19 years old, and Qian Xiaolan, 17 years old, a relative of his fellow villager Shi Zengshou, were both female workers in the mill. They went to work at the factory at 6:00 PM on the 29th of last month, but neither returned home the next morning. People were sent out to search for them in all directions, but no information was found. The day before yesterday, it was learned that Fei Changhe and Chen Changfu, two Taixing people residing in a bungalow at the corner of Linqing Road and Jingzhou Road with no number, were related to the disappearance of Li Zhang and Qian Xiaolan. Yangshupu Police Station dispatched detective Zhang Degong to secretly investigate and arrested Fei and Chen at the address. They were taken into custody at the police station and sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court yesterday morning. According to police lawyer Zhang Tianyin's accusation, Chen Changfu confessed at the police station that on the evening of the 29th of last month, he saw Fei Changhe escorting Li Zhang and Qian Xiaolan on a tram to a certain place. According to Fei, Li Zhang had been having an affair with Chen Changhe for many years and had a special relationship. They were mutually shirking responsibility. It is requested that the case be postponed. Then, according to the victims Li Wanxi and Shi Zengshou, they stated the circumstances, and Li Wanxi also stated that he had not witnessed whether his wife Zhang had illicit affairs with Chen Changfu, but he had heard people say that they had opened a room and slept together in a certain hotel, but there was no conclusive evidence. When questioned, the two defendants were evasive and claimed that they did not know who had abducted Li Zhang and Qian Xiaolan. Please investigate. After Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confession, he ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation at a later date.

A Child on a Rickshaw 164

Without the Ability to Hire a Rickshaw

And Without a Destination

At 5:40 PM the other day, Wang Chunjiang, a policeman at post No. 24 of the Second Precinct, found a rickshaw with a boy about five or six years old sitting on it at Xiaoximen. He immediately asked the rickshaw puller where he had picked up the boy and where he was pulling him. According to the rickshaw puller, Tang Changyuan, the child got on the rickshaw on Shigaota Road and told him to pull him to Yuqingli. Since the rickshaw puller should not have taken the young child alone and had no destination, it was suspected that he was abducting the child. They were immediately detained. According to Zhang, the director, the child confessed that his name was Wang Genfu and he did not know his age, origin, or address. He only said that he got on the rickshaw on Baoshan Road and had no ability to hire a rickshaw. He was suspected of abduction and was to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for review.

Jiufeng News, Second Issue Published 172

Some unscrupulous thugs coveted the mud and stone in the mountains of Songqing Jiufeng. They privately mined them, seeking only private gain and disregarding public welfare. They blasted the bones and destroyed the scenic spots. The anger of the people was hard to express in words. After repeated appeals from local gentry and famous people in the government and the public, the relevant departments of the Ministry of Interior, Industry, and Finance issued a clear ban at the same time. The fellow villagers in Shanghai feared that the embers would reignite and secretly planned to take further action, advocating strict supervision to prevent them from being taken advantage of again. Therefore, the history of Jiufeng and the achievements of the local gentry in protecting the mountain this time must be publicized in a timely manner to commemorate it. Thus, Jiufeng News was created. The second issue was published yesterday, and the content is richer than before. The office has moved to the Songshun Rice Shop building on Ximin Tinyin Road, Dashijie Road. Those who want to read it can attach a one-cent postage stamp and it will be sent to them.

Shenbao Reader Communication Regulations 180

The staff of this newspaper firmly believes that readers have several personal questions that urgently need to be resolved. Based on the spirit of serving society, we are willing to take the position of consultant and sincerely discuss these questions in writing. If readers can obtain appropriate solutions, reduce difficulties, and increase happiness, wouldn't that be delightful?

1. The questions that readers want to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are temporarily limited to three categories: education, occupation, and marriage.

2. When communicating, please first state your surname, given name, gender, age, occupation (or place of study, grade), origin, and mailing address (it is advisable to continue to provide details when communicating, as we are afraid that previous letters may not have been delivered). After that, start a new paragraph to indicate the questions you want to discuss. The text should be detailed, accurate, and easy for people to understand the true meaning. Please write "Reader Communication Department of Shenbao" on the outside of the envelope. Include a sufficient number of return postage stamps.

3. When communicating, you must cut out the special imprint of the Shenbao Reader Communication column and paste it in the upper left corner of the letter as a voucher.

4. The methods for handling letters received by this newspaper A. Respect readers' wishes. If the letter states that you wish to have your questions answered privately or that you do not want your name to be disclosed when answering, we will comply.

B. If the letter does not state how to answer, but the staff believes that answering one person has the value of providing a reference for everyone, it should be disclosed in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states that you wish to have your questions answered in the newspaper, but the space is limited, we can only disclose the main points or even fail to disclose them, or because the questions are still under consideration, we have to delay the disclosure. Please forgive us. However, if we cannot answer in the newspaper, we will still answer by letter.

Free Talk

Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai Fu Tan Hui (Talks by the Studio Owner Who Doesn't Remove Garden Weeds)

Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai Fu (The Studio Owner Who Doesn't Remove Garden Weeds) 181

Several years ago, I saw a couplet written by Zeng Guofan. First, I looked at the lower line, which was: (Love to raise fish in pots to understand the mechanism of transformation). I didn't think much of it. Because the free world of fish is the river, the lake, the sea; where can't you understand their mechanism of transformation, why do you have to catch the lively fish into the pot? The pot is the fish's prison; the potted fish is a prisoner who has been put on shackles and tortured. Now, abandoning the greatness of the river, the lake, and the sea, and pursuing the mechanism of creation in a small prison-style pot is not only against nature but also shows the narrowness of the measure. I have always been against raising birds in cages, so I unconsciously developed a deep dissatisfaction with raising fish in pots. I took this dissatisfied attitude to look at the upper line. I saw the upper line wrote: (Don't remove the garden grass to keep business alive), I couldn't help but exclaim a few times, happy to forget all the dissatisfaction in my heart. From then on, I wanted to use this meaning to build a studio, calling it Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai (The Studio That Doesn't Remove Garden Weeds). But how can people who are eating breakfast worrying about dinner have extra money to build a house? Taking a step back, if the owner of the studio can't be made, why not be a Zhaifu (studio owner)? Okay, let's put it this way, forgive me for self-appointing the title of Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhaifu. People who need a Zhaifu, please see this name clearly; otherwise, if you want to remove the grass and I don't remove the grass, what will happen if it gets stiff?

An Account of Fang Bingling's Meritorious Pacification of the Japanese Pirates 182

— Cai Liang

Jinshan is located in a remote coastal area. The local customs are simple and honest. Its old county seat was called Kangcheng, which is also the hometown of the former Nanjing Mayor, He Minhun. During the Jiajing period of the late Ming Dynasty, whenever there was a good harvest, Japanese pirates would cross the sea to harass the area at will. By the time the government troops arrived after hearing the news, they would have already looted their fill and left, treating the massacre of our people as a common occurrence. At that time, there was a local named Fang Bingling who lamented the unbridled actions of the Japanese pirates and was eager to find a way to suppress their arrogance. Therefore, he spent all his personal wealth to build a city wall as a defense. He also established local militia and set up defensive works such as bows and arrows in preparation for emergencies. Before several months had passed, the Japanese pirates arrived again and looted as before. Fang Gong then led the militia and fought them bravely. As soon as they engaged, the Japanese pirates were defeated and nearly half of them were captured. They were greatly frightened, knelt down, and begged to surrender. Fang Gong refused and annihilated them all. Thus, the Japanese pirate threat subsided. Subsequently, the matter was reported to the imperial court, and there was talk of a significant reward. However, before the honorable decree could be issued, Fang Gong suddenly died of a sudden illness. Once the news spread, there was shock and grief both above and below. The people of the county mourned him deeply, and some even wore mourning clothes for him, as they believed that without him, the area would have been devastated. Fang Gong sacrificed himself for the area, spending his family fortune to alleviate the disaster, displaying a truly awe-inspiring sense of righteousness, rarely matched in historical records. Subsequently, it was unanimously agreed that his virtues should not be forgotten. Therefore, they raised funds to build a temple to honor his spirit and inscribed his deeds on a stone tablet. More than three hundred years have passed since then, but the temple remains new. Sacrifices are offered every year without fail. Moreover, during the Ghost Festival in the lunar calendar, there is always a grand incense gathering. At that time, visitors come from near and far. Even wandering performers seek it out as if they were in great fear of missing it. For example, fortune tellers from Shanghai, such as Wu Jianguang and Ni Tianhong, all travel there without fear of hardship to pay their respects sincerely. Some say that Fang Gong was also one of their kind. Although the truth of this is uncertain, it is truly extraordinary for an ordinary person to receive such respect from later generations. I wonder if those who hold high positions and receive generous salaries today will be moved by this?

Research on the Clown Character 183

— Lu Shifang

"Clown" is the name of a theatrical role, commonly known as "painted face." The performer uses humor and exaggeration, with every movement and gesture designed to make people laugh. As for the origin of the name, some say that during the reign of Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty, people from all over the country came to court. The emperor ordered actors to imitate them in a play, hence the name "Chou Jiao" (clown role). " 儔 " and " 丑 " are homophones, so it was abbreviated to "丑" (chou). However, when I read the History of Ming, during the reign of Emperor Xianzong of the Ming Dynasty, the eunuch Wang Zhi colluded with Wang Yue and Chen Yue, forming a close-knit group that held immense power and aroused widespread resentment. There was a eunuch named A Chou who was skilled at humor and often performed short plays before the emperor, which often contained veiled criticism. One day, A Chou pretended to be drunk and behaved drunkenly. He first sent someone to announce, "An official has arrived!" He continued to curse and scold as before. Then it was announced, "The emperor has arrived!" He continued to curse and scold as before. When it was announced, "Eunuch Wang has arrived!" the drunk was immediately startled and became submissive. Someone nearby asked, "You are not afraid of the emperor's arrival, but you are afraid of Eunuch Wang. Why?" He replied, "I only know there is Eunuch Wang, but I do not know there is an emperor." Another day, he suddenly imitated Wang Zhi's attire, holding two axes and walking quickly. When asked why, he replied, "I am leading troops, and I rely on these two axes." When asked what the axes were called, he said, "Wang Yue and Chen Yue." The emperor smiled slightly. From then on, Wang Zhi's favor gradually declined, and he was soon dismissed. Later generations thought that A Chou could move the emperor and make him realize the truth, like Dongfang Shuo and Chun Yuyi of the Han dynasty. Therefore, they imitated him in plays and named the role after him, and thus the name "clown" was established. I do not know which of these two explanations is correct. In my opinion, the former explanation is far-fetched and contrived, while the latter is more credible and has evidence.

Tidbits 184

— (Juan)

Yesterday, I met a friend who has been immersed in the sea of love for twenty years. I do not know what stimulated him, but he said the following words to me. (I do not want to commit suicide alone. That death is too cowardly. I do not want to force my lover to die with me. That death is too despicable. If only I had a three-foot-long sword to travel the world and kill all the lovely women, eradicating the root of love, to prevent harm to young people and the ruination of their lives. Then, I would laugh heartily and die generously. But I do not have that ability. The last resort is to pray sincerely that a comet will collide with the Earth, shattering it into nothingness, so that men, women, sentient beings, and insentient beings can all perish together. Would not that be clean? Would not that be refreshing?)

Zheng Wuchang's Return from Rambling 185

— Dan Lin

Zheng Wuchang of Sheng County is known for his poetry and painting. He is skilled in landscapes, flowers, and female figures. His landscape paintings are majestic and lush, with the influence of the Song and Yuan dynasties. Song Bolu, a senior official in Guanzhong, praised his collection of paintings highly. In May, Zheng Wuchang, at the invitation of his friend Zhao Xuequan (Guantao), the military commander, traveled to the provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi. He visited historical sites and explored secluded spots wherever he went, touring all the famous places of the Yangtze and Huai Rivers. He returned to Shanghai a few days ago. I made an appointment to chat with him over tea. When asked about the contents of his travel bag, he smiled and said, "I have something." He then opened his suitcase and showed me two paper scrolls. One was a collection of seventy-nine sketches, all composed on the spot. Among them, the scenes such as "Crossing the Lion River," "Riding a Donkey at the Ferry," "Mysterious Moon in Wusheng," "Buddha's Hand Embracing Clouds," "Discussing Military Affairs at the Yellow Temple," and "Rain Blocking the Green Clouds" were particularly unique in their perspectives. The other was a collection of one hundred and thirty-four poems, titled "Spicy Grass" (borrowing from Xinwei). Most of them were works that commemorated ancient times on the spot. I love his poem "Staying at the Yuan Family's Mansion": "The warm sun shines through half the window, people wake up early, gentle breeze rustles through the tall willows, and birds sing." Tengwang Pavilion: "Autumn waters and sunset clouds, the land of talented scholars, beam clouds and curtain rain, the beautiful residence of officials." (The pavilion is now a water police station.) Traveling: "The stream and mountains often allow for spiritual excursions, poetry and wine gradually become estranged from the taste of travel." The Tomb of Bada Shanren: "A generation of rivers and mountains leaves behind ink plays, carelessly remember the wind and rain remembering crazy poems." A heart for patriotism is as bright as the moon, but there is no place to stand, only the blue of the clouds. The language is leisurely, and the thoughts are clear, making them enjoyable to savor. Zheng Wuchang, upon returning to Shanghai, lives a secluded life. Except for seeing two or three close friends, he avoids social engagements. It seems that he is deeply in debt with his paintings since the past three months. He is buried in writing and painting every day, sweating and painting until midnight before going to bed. However, his style is now more profound and robust than before.

Two Lions Appear 186

— Ming Long

Since the previous torrential rains caused disaster in the capital, and floods inundated the area, the area outside Yijiang Gate in Xiaguan was a vast expanse of water due to its proximity to the Yangtze River. Traffic was suspended. The area outside Xingzhong Gate and along Jiangbian Avenue was also ankle-deep in water. Autumn waters were connected to the sky. The Four Elephants Bridge in Confucius Temple in the south of the city, and the Hongwu Street and Chengxian Street in the Four Archways in the north of the city, have been flooded for more than a month, and the situation has not subsided slightly. On the night of the 25th, the rain was heavy, and the wind was strong. The rivers and lakes rose sharply, and the floodwaters increased further. The people suffered calamity. Many places on Zhongshan Avenue were also flooded. Therefore, the Municipal Works Bureau has recently been hiring workers day and night on the sidewalks along Section 2 of the road to dig trenches and install water pipes to facilitate drainage and maintain road administration. Yesterday, workers in front of the First Police Station of the Daxing Palace excavated a large, ancient, mottled stone lion from the soil. About 500 steps away to the east (in front of the Eastern District Experimental School), another similar stone lion was excavated. It is said that they are one male and one female, similar to the lions in front of the National Government (also very close). However, it is impossible to investigate when they were submerged in the soil. The most interesting thing is that they both emerged from the soil at the same time without any prior agreement. It is truly a strange event.

Miscellaneous Notes from Japan 187

— Ai Ai, sent from Tokyo

Seeing Ms. Kinue Hitomi's Love Letter

The death of Ms. Kinue Hitomi, the Japanese track and field prodigy who set the world's highest record, has already been reported in this newspaper. The death of such a vibrant and vigorous young woman has undoubtedly earned the tears of many sympathizers.

Among the 80 million Japanese men and women today, the only people known to the world besides Marshal Togo are Ms. Hitomi. Unexpectedly, the old man remains energetic as ever, while Ms. Hitomi has already passed away. This is truly a great loss to the Japanese sports world.

The news of Ms. Hitomi's premature death has spread throughout the world. The Women's International Athletic Federation held a memorial service for her in Paris. At the opening of the British local representative women's track and field sports meeting, everyone remained silent for one minute to pray for her. Women's and sports circles in Germany, the United States, Switzerland, and the Netherlands have sent telegrams to express their condolences. Zhang Xueliang, the young general and deputy commander who loves sports in our country, also sent a telegram to express his condolences. The number of wreaths given by all walks of life is countless. The Okayama City Education Association has prepared to build a bronze statue for Ms. Hitomi to commemorate this female hero. The 12th of this month was the day of Ms. Hitomi's funeral. More than 10,000 people went to help carry the coffin. Ms. Hitomi is truly the first woman to receive such mourning and honor.

Ms. Hitomi was still an engaged woman. In 1928, when Ms. Hitomi returned from the Ninth International Olympics in The Hague, Netherlands, there were rumors in society that Ms. Hitomi would marry a certain young man. But the result did not materialize. Many lads who admired Ms. Hitomi often wrote letters to Ms. Hitomi recommending themselves. But they were all rejected. At first, some people said that Ms. Hitomi already had another (dessert). (Dessert means sweetheart) However, the general public thought that this was a rumor made by disgruntled young people and could not believe it. Unexpectedly, after Ms. Hitomi's death, in her diary on her sickbed, a unfinished love letter was found. It was full of tenderness and sorrow. One can imagine that the heartbroken person must have been devastated when reading this letter.

(My G that I miss. I'm really bored. If I can't overcome the disease early and jump out of this prison-like hospital, I don't know when I can communicate freely with you. Wasn't that on Tuesday afternoon? Maybe it was on Monday afternoon. When I was in a daze, my nurse, Hanako, took a light green letter shell, wanting to step into my room. But she immediately received an indication from my mother sitting by my bed and withdrew.

The doctor rejected the guests who came to visit me. He didn't let me read all my friends' letters. Also, I was forbidden to write to any friend. They thought this was the only magic method to make the patient quiet. But they will never know that your letter is my more effective medicine.

I have been suffering from insomnia lately. The desolate moonlight last night shone on my window bars, causing me to recall last year. Recalling last year, we were talking deeply in a moonlit night. G, what a memorable night.

The day before yesterday, my sister came to Osaka from my hometown to see me. She is a virtuous wife and mother, with cute children and a sweet family. In her conversation, she seemed to feel sad for my life. It seemed that my life was too boring and lonely. But G, I am used to being lonely.

The above was written on May 25. Another ten days have passed. In these ten days, my illness has made good progress. The doctor said that according to the current situation, if there is no change, I can be discharged from the hospital by the end of June. Then we can meet in Tokyo at the end of July. July. July that I look forward to.

G. Have you ever gone home? I am so sorry. I often trouble you to worry about me. Now I am getting better soon. I will definitely get better. G, take care of yourself. You have to work hard.)

Confident that fame and fortune are my duty as a concubine, I will leave all my beauty for you to enjoy. Unexpectedly, good things take time. Now, it has become a proverb. This unposted suicide note is really good material for a sad love story.

Speaking of Club Rotary

A Husband's Wife (2) 188

— Jiang Hongjiao

In recent times, the atmosphere in this house has only been tense, hazy, acrid, and indescribably sharp and discordant. The old harmony, happiness,

Sweetness, all gone. Every night, regardless of whether the northwest wind was blowing, it was raining or snowing, or it was very cold and there was no stove in the room, Mrs. Li always sat dully waiting for her husband to come home. She knew that she might find some needlework to do to relieve the loneliness, but the reality was often the opposite of the ideal. Because she was eagerly awaiting her husband, she took the scissors and cut the clothes, and maybe she would cut her pants. She should sew tight stitches, but maybe she would sew them sparsely, and even the needle would pierce her fingers, and she would not even realize that the fresh blood had stained her new clothes, so she simply did not do it, and simply sat dully, concentrating, listening, and paying attention to whether there were any vehicles or pedestrians outside the door. She was used to hearing her husband's footsteps and was very familiar with them, so the distant footsteps would often make her surprised and approach, and finally disappoint her. The pendulum of the clock swings so balanced and evenly to advance the time, it is very boring to listen to; the sound of the wind in the courtyard is like a lion's roar, hitting the building windows, shaking the house a little. In addition to resenting her husband for betraying the fragrant quilt, she was also worried about whether he was very safe outside.

Recently, Mr. Li's mind has been very unsettled, almost restless.

How could his wife not see it. He was often absent-minded, very silent, his smiles and words were several times fewer than usual, and his appetite also decreased. He was definitely not someone without something on his mind. Mrs. Li sat dully in the lonely cold night, often guessing the reason for her husband's changed attitude. Is it A? Is it B? Or is it C…D…E…? She thought carefully about each item, but could not get a definite answer; then she thought about whether she had done something, or whether that sentence made him feel unhappy? But she could not find the slightest trace that would make him feel so tired of the family. Among the many hypothetical questions, she was more sure that the cause of the love incident was the majority. So she thought about the impact of her husband falling in love with another woman. His body was weakened, his economy was tight, his family was broken, and all his prospects for advancement were hindered and stagnated. This is such a dangerous phenomenon! She was worried about the happiness of him and her now and in the future, and it was so precarious that her weak heart trembled almost to pieces.

Bond Market's Trend Towards Lull Lingers

Yesterday, in the bond market, futures for the twenty-year salt tax treasury bonds were opened for trading. However, because this particular treasury bond is still relatively uncommon in the current market, activity was extremely minimal. Other bonds also continued to be quite quiet, with spot transactions as scarce as before. As for the trend of various bonds yesterday, the morning market was better, with most rebounding slightly. The afternoon market saw buying interest wane, and prices subsequently fell again, fluctuating by about six or seven jiao between the morning and afternoon markets. As a result, compared to the previous day, there were mixed gains and losses, with the number only around two or three jiao. Total spot transactions for the day amounted to 5,000 yuan, and futures transactions totaled over 10 million yuan for both morning and afternoon markets, with the consolidated tax accounting for about half of that, it is said.

Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Leans Heavily Towards Downstream 195

The yarn market is trending downstream again. The slump in the overseas cotton yarn situation is particularly severe, leading to nervousness and a market decline. However, new sellers are not seen as being particularly active. Nevertheless, major players are still not taking steps to hedge, so the market is still stable. The forces of both buyers and sellers are exerting considerable pressure, and actual demand in the market is still being maintained. The Yunnan and Sichuan factions have not given up on their intentions, it is said.

▲Human Standard Falls by One or Two Taels At the opening of the human standard market, the sharp fall in American cotton caused popular sentiment to dissipate and the market situation to be particularly weak. Each month fell by one or two taels to one tael and one qian. In the afternoon, the price of Grade 3 yarn fell sharply, but the local market was not affected, and each month rose slightly by one or two qian. Transaction statistics totaled 17,700 bales. Enquiries revealed that 950 bales were bought from Yiyu, 550 bales from Tongyu, and 400 bales from Gongtai. Yu Da bought 600 bales, Rongxing 1,000 bales, and Yichang 550 bales. Cotton Market Plunge Begins Abruptly 196

The cotton market has suddenly weakened, and the plunge is severe, due to a significant drop in American cotton, causing panic. Many are closing out positions, and the market is increasingly weak. However, most major bullish players have not yet taken action, because the flooding is severe, and Hankou has suffered considerable damage. Therefore, the Hankou faction is instead buying long positions in Shanghai, so the local market situation is still robust. However, the global situation is still weakening, it is said.

▲Hankou Standard Plunges by Half a Tael At the opening of the Exchange's Hankou Standard market, the trend of falling American cotton caused nervousness, and selling pressure was stronger.
